出自tedxboston這個開放的演講中 , 理查德・雷斯尼克告訴我們基因測序是如何廉價並快速得顛覆醫療體制 。	in an open talk at tedx boston , richard resnick told us how genome sequencing is cheap and rapidly disrupting health systems .
dna , biotech , healthcare , science , technology	dna , biotech , healthcare , he's doing it .
理查德・雷斯尼克:歡迎進入基因革命時代	richard risnyk: welcome to the age of genetic revolution .
女士們先生們 , 我向您展示人類基因組	ladies and gentlemen , i'll show you the human genome .
左上是一號染色體	on the left is the chromosome number one .
右下是性染色體	here's a sex chromosome .
女性有兩條那個大大的x染色體男性有個x當然 , 還有個小小的y	women have two big x chromosomes , men have an x and , of course , a little y .
男士們 , 不好意思 , 就是那個小東西讓你不同	guys , sorry , that little thing makes you different .
如果放大這條基因組你看到的當然就是這個雙螺旋結構生命的密碼就是由這些生化的字母組成或者說鹼基 , 對吧:a , c , g和t	if you zoom in on this genome , of course you see the code of this double helix , of life , is made of these biochemical letters , or base , right , a , c , g and t .
人類基因組有多少這樣的結構 ? 30億	how much does the human genome have ? three billion .

這個更大的結構可以讓我們預測那些實際存在卻沒有被觀察到的粒子	this much larger configuration allows us to predict particles that are actually not observed .
這個統一模型推測出了這兩種新子對應的粒子它們應該和弱力很相似但是效果更弱	this unification model suggests that these two new particles should be similar to the weak force , but they're even weaker .
現在可以在七維空間中旋轉這個載荷集同時考慮一下關於粒子的奇怪現象:在六維載荷空間中物質的第二代和第三代擁有和第一代物質相同的載荷	now we can rotate this episode in seven dimensions , and consider the strange phenomenon of matter in sixdimensional charge space: the second and third generations of matter have the same charges as the first generation .
這些粒子透過對應的六個載荷無法一一識別	these particles can't identify by corresponding to six charges .
在標準載荷空間上他們會彼此疊加	in a standard charge space , they overlap each other .
然而在八維載荷空間中我們可以賦予每一個粒子唯一的新載荷	but in eightdimensional charge spaces , we can give each particle the only new charge .
然後在八維空間中旋轉看看整體的圖案是什麼樣的	and then rotate in eight dimensions and see what the overall pattern looks like .
這裡我們可以看到物質的第二代和第三代透過一種叫 " 三重性 " 對稱和第一代相關聯	here we can see the second and third generations of matter connected through a symmetry called " symmetry " with the first generation .
在八維中的這個特殊的載荷圖案是數學中最為漂亮的幾何結構之一	this particular charge pattern in eight dimensions is one of the most beautiful geometric structures in mathematics .
這是最大的例外型李群e8的圖案	this is the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .
李群是光滑曲線形的248維空間	lie groups are 248dimensional spaces for smooth curves .
圖案的每一點都能這個極其複雜而又美麗的圖案中找到對稱點	every point of the pattern can be found in this incredibly complicated , beautiful pattern .
e8中的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦廣義相對論中用來解釋重力的扭曲時空	a small portion of the e8 can be used to describe the distortion of gravity in einstein's general theory of relativity .
這個幾何形狀和量子力學一起能夠以最小的尺度描述萬物之理	together with this geometric shape and quantum mechanics , we can describe everything at the smallest scales .
而在八維載荷空間中的這個圖案顯得異常美麗它還囊括了上千種這些基本粒子之間可能的相互作用每一種作用只是這個複雜形狀的一個平面	and this pattern in the eightdimensional charge space shows an extraordinary beauty , and it includes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which acts as a complex shape .
轉動它時可以看到包含其中的很多錯綜複雜的圖案	and as it rotates , you can see a lot of the intricate patterns embedded in them .
透過某種旋轉我們可以在八維空間沿一個對稱軸方向觀察這個圖案並且一次看盡所有粒子	through some kind of spin , we can look at this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .
這是個很美的結構和其他統一理論一樣我們可以看到在這個圖案中有一些空格需要新的粒子來填補	it's a beautiful unification , just like any other theory , and we can see that there's some empty space in this pattern that needs new particles to be filled .
在這有20個空格需要新粒子來填補其中兩個已有帕蒂和薩拉姆粒子填補	in this space there are 20 new particles that need to be filled , two of which have been filled with patty and salam particles .
從圖案的位置我們知道這些新粒子和希格斯粒子一樣存在於標量場中但是它們擁有色荷且和強力相互作用	from the location of the pattern , we know that these new particles are like the higgs particles in the quantum field , but they have color charge and interact with strong forces .
填入這些新粒子使圖案完整讓我們得到完整的e8	we filled these new particles to complete the patterns , and we got the full e8 .
這個e8圖案有著深厚的數學根基	this e8 pattern contains a thick mathematical root .
在數學界中它被很多人認為是最美麗的結構	in mathematics , it's seen as the most beautiful structure that a lot of people think .
有人預言這個擁有無比數學美的結構能夠以我們可以想象到的最小尺寸描述粒子相互作用的真相	some people predict that this structure with incredibly mathematical beauty can describe the fact that particles interact at the smallest scale .
而這個數學描述自然的理論並不是剛剛出來的	and this mathematical theory of describing nature is not just coming out .
1623年伽利略寫道: " 大自然這本一直展示在我們面前的書是用數學的語言寫的	in 1623 , galileo wrote , " nature has been shown in front of us in the language of mathematics .
它由三角形圓形和其他幾何形狀組成沒有了這些東西在人力所及的範圍裡我們根本不能瞭解沒有了這些我們會迷失在黑暗的迷宮中 "	it's made up of triangles , circles and other geometric shapes , and we can't understand these things in the human range , and we can't understand them , and we'll miss them in the dark labyrinth . "
我相信這是真的我曾試過按照伽利略的指導只用三角形圓形和其他的幾何形狀去描述量子物理的數學性	i believe this is true . i tried to follow galileo's guidance using only triangle circles and other geometric shapes to describe the mathematics of quantum physics .
當我和其他物理學家在研究這些東西時數學就像一個黑暗的迷宮	and while other physicists and i were studying these things , mathematics was like a dark labyrinth .
但是我們確信數學的核心是純粹美麗的幾何學	but we do believe that at the heart of mathematics is purely beautiful geometry .
數學和量子力學一起把我們的宇宙描述為一個在成長的e8珊瑚同時粒子在每個可能的位置相互作用展現出美麗的圖案	together , mathematics and quantum mechanics describe our universe as a growing e8 coral , and particles interact in each position to show beautiful patterns .
藉助大型強子對撞機之類的新型機器圖案得到進一步豐富我們可能看到到底e8圖案還是另一種圖案反映了自然的本質	with new machine patterns like the large hadron collider , we get further rich , and we might see e8 patterns or other patterns reflect the nature of nature .
這個探索過程是一個奇妙的探險	this process of exploration is a wonderful adventure .
如果對撞機發現了符合e8圖案的粒子那可太酷了	if the lhc finds particles that fit e8 patterns , that's pretty cool .
如果對撞機發現了新粒子但不符合這個圖案那會非常有趣雖然對e8理論不利	if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit into this pattern , that's very interesting , although theory is bad for e8 .
而且在一定程度上對我不利	and in a way , it was bad for me .
那到底有多不利呢 ?	how bad is that ?
恩那是十分的不利啊	well , that's very bad .
但推測大自然的運作總是很冒險的	but it's an adventurous thing to do .
這個理論和其他這型別的理論都是在下大注	this theory , along with other theories , is massively focused .
即使花很多精力取得很多成果也不一定能得出自然的真理	even with a lot of effort , it doesn't necessarily come out of nature .
理論物理就是這樣失敗是很常見的	that's how theoretical physics failed .
這樣看來新物理理論就像新開的公司	in this way , new physics theories are like startups .
巨大投資後對那些失敗的嘗試情感上總會難以割捨	after enormous investments , emotionally difficult to get rid of those failures .
但在科學界如果沒有用就要丟掉它再試試別的	but in science , if it doesn't work , throw it away and try something else .
而在這些不確定中唯一能夠保持理智並獲得幸福的方法是在生活中保持平衡和明察事理	and in these uncertainties , the only way to be rational and acquire happiness is to remain balanced and inspected in life .
我已經儘可能保持生活的平衡了	i've remained as balanced as possible .
我試著在物理愛情和衝浪中尋找平衡就是我三個載荷的方向	i tried to balance my own three charges in physical love and surfing directions .
這樣就算我的物理研究沒有任何成果我依然擁有美好的生活	so even if my physics didn't work , i still had a good life .
我試著在風景優美的地方居住	i'm trying to live in beautiful places .
過去十年我大部分時間都住在毛伊島一個超級漂亮的地方	i've spent the last 10 years living on the island of maui , a beautiful place .
現在我父母最大的謎團是我是怎樣在沒有一個全職工作的情況下活下來的	now , my parents' biggest mystery is how i survived without a fulltime job .
我要告訴你們這個秘密	i'm going to tell you this secret .
這是我在毛伊島上的家庭辦公室的照片	this is a picture of my family's office on maui .
你們可能注意到這些照片似曾相似但背景稍有不同	you may notice that these images were similar , but backgrounds were slightly different .
因為這曾經是我在毛伊島的家和辦公室	because this was my home and office in maui .
我選擇了一種不同尋常的生活	i chose a different kind of life .
不擔心房租讓我把時間花在喜歡做的事情上	not worrying about rent let me spend my time doing what i like to do .
流浪的生活方式有時會很艱難也正因此我才能可生活在美麗的地方維持我所喜歡的平衡的生活	living a nomadic lifestyle can sometimes be hard , and because of that , i was able to live in beautiful places to keep my life balanced .
我可以花大量的時間在超級聰明的珊瑚上	i could spend a lot of time on superintelligent corals .
同時我也很樂意和超級聰明的人打交道	and at the same time , i would love to talk to hyperintelligent people .
很高興能被邀請到這兒演講	it's great to be invited here .
我想我只懂了百分之二的部分 , 但是我絕對喜歡它 。 所以我想獻一下醜 。	i think i only know two percent , but i absolutely like it . so i want to give it a little ugly .
你的萬物理論...我喜歡稱之為珊瑚理論	your theory of everything i like to call it coral .
好吧 , 它讓人們興奮的原因是如果你是對的 , 那就把重力和量子理論結合了起來 。	well , the reason it gets people excited is if you're right , it combines gravity and quantum theory .
所以你是不是說我們應該瞭解在宇宙中那些最微小的事物有可能就是e8模型 ?	so are you saying that we should understand that the tiniest thing in the universe might be e8 ?
我是說 , 你心裡是不是有一個最小的尺寸 , 還是.... ?	i mean , do you have a minimum size in your mind or . . .
嗯 , 剛剛給你們看得圖案就是我們所知的基本粒子物理 , 而且它已經是一個很漂亮的圖案了 。	well , the pattern i showed you earlier is what we know about the elementary particle physics , and it's already a beautiful pattern .
那個就是我所說的我們很確信的地方 。	and that's what i'm talking about . we're pretty sure .
而這個形狀和e8有著明顯的相似處 , 在剩下的圖片中幾乎和e8合為一體 。	and this shape has a remarkable similarity to e8 , and the rest of the picture is almost associated with the e8 .
我給你們看得這些點狀圖案實際上代表著高維物體的對稱性 , 這些圖案在我們生活的時空中 , 蜷曲 , 移動和舞蹈 。	i'm showing you these spot patterns that actually represent the symmetries of highdimensional objects that curl up and move and dance in spacetimes in which we live .
這就解釋了所有的我們所看見的基本粒子 。	and this explains all the elementary particles that we see .
克里斯:但是就我的理解 , 弦理論家會在更小的弦震動裡解釋電子--我知道你不喜歡弦理論 。	ca: but in my understanding , string theorists explain electrons in smaller string vibrations i know you don't like string theory .
但我們該怎樣理解在e8模型中的電子 ?	but how do we understand electrons in e8 ?
加勒特:不 , 它將會是這個e8型狀對稱性的一部分 。	gk: no , it's going to be part of this e8shaped symmetry .
所以實際上 , 當這個形狀在時空中游走 , 它會扭曲 。 而它扭曲的方向就是我們所看到的粒子 。 所以就是--e8形狀的大小 , 是怎麼樣和電子相聯絡的呢 ?	so actually , when this shape is swimming through spacetime , it's distorting , and it's distorting directions that are the particles that we see , so it's the size of the e8 shape , how is it contacting the electrons ?
我自己有些想象不出來 。	i can't think of myself .
它會大些還是小些 ?	is it bigger or smaller ?
嗯 , 就我們所知電子是點粒子 , 所以這個會讓我們看到最小的尺寸 。	well , the electrons , as we know them , are point particles , so this one shows us the smallest scale .
所以在量子場論中 , 這些東西的解釋方式是所有的可能性都在同時展開發展 。	so in the quantum field theory , the explanation of these things is that all possibilities are unfolding at the same time .
這也是我為什麼拿珊瑚作類比 。	that's why i'm analogizing corals .
因為這樣 , e8的進入方式是一個可以連線時空中每一點的形狀 。	because of that , the way e8 comes in is it's a shape that connects every bit of spacetime .
還有 , 想我所說的 , 形狀在經過這個曲線的表面時它的扭曲的方式和其的扭曲方向是基本粒子它們自己 。	and , as i said , the shape twists the way that it twists on the surface of this curve and the way the elementary particles twist themselves .
所以根據量子場論 , 它們自己把放大到和點一樣 , 然後相互作用 。	so according to quantum field theory , they zoom in on themselves and interact with each other .
我不知道我能不能解釋得更加清楚了 。	i don't know if i can explain that better .
克里斯:沒關係 。	ca: that's ok .

黑猩猩在晚上睡覺前就是這麼打招呼的	that's how the chimpanzees greet up until they sleep at night .
你聽見這種叫聲從山谷這頭傳到那頭從一群猩猩窩傳到另一群猩猩窩	you're hearing this call from the valley , and it goes from one group of chimpanzees to another group of chimpanzees .
我今晚的演講想從澤雷•阿蘭希格昨天留下的話題開始	i want to start this evening with jersey alanshig yesterday .
他談的是這個令人驚異的靈長類幼仔 , 叫selam , 三歲大	he was talking about this incredible primate , selam , threeyearold primate .
我們還聽了透過測繪dna基因所得的人類的歷史和族譜	we've also heard the history and family trees of the human dna gene by mapping the dna gene .
已故古生物學家路易斯•李奇是他把我引上研究黑猩猩之路的	the late paleontologist louis leakey was the way he introduced me to chimpanzees .
回顧過去 , 這條路實在不同尋常	it's a very unusual path to look back in the past .
現在看來比較普通可他的論據是 , 因為他曾尋找在非洲的早期人類化石遺蹟	now it looks more general , but his argument is that he looked for the early human fossil miracles in africa .
這些化石上 , 從附屬肌肉的形狀上 , 對於那些早期人類的模樣像什麼都能給研究者很多啟示從由他們身邊發現的原始工具上可以看出一些關於他們生活方式的端倪	these fossils , from the shape of the possessional muscle , can give researchers a lot of revelations , and from the primitive tools that they've discovered around them , you can tell a little bit about their lifestyle .
但他們的行為表現是什麼樣的 ? 這是他想知道的	but what does their behavior look like ? this is what he wanted to know .
當然 , 行為沒有在化石裡體現	of course , behavior doesn't embody the fossils .
他辨稱如果我們發現當代人類在行為模式上與和其最相近的物種巨猿相似或者相同那麼或許這些行為在大概七百萬年前在似猿似人的祖先身上存在過	he recognized that if we discovered modern humans , like their most australopithecines , or australopithecines , then maybe these behaviors existed in an apelike ancestor about seven million years ago .
因此 , 也許我們身上的那些行為特徵是從遠古時代傳下來的	so , maybe the behavioral features that we have in our bodies have come from ancient times .
噢 , 如果你看一下現在講人類進化的書就會常常發現 , 人們是基於黑猩猩的行為表現來思考早期人類可能的行為方式	oh , if you look at the book of human evolution now , it turns out that people are based on the behavior of chimpanzees to think about how early humans might behave .
與別的存活動物相比 , 他們更像我們這一點我在這次ted會議中聽到過	they were more like us than any other activist , which i've heard at this ted conference .
所以我今天要講的就是黑猩猩是在其行為方式的與人類的相似點	so what i'm going to talk about today is that chimpanzees behave like humans in their behavior .
每個黑猩猩都有他/她自己的個性	every chimpanzee has himself or her personality .
當然 , 我給他們起名字 。 他們能活60歲或者更長儘管我們覺得他們中的絕大多數在野生環境活不到60歲	of course , i give them names . they live 60 years , or they live longer , although we think the vast majority of them live under 60 .
這是wurzel猩猩 。 母猩猩在11或12歲時生第一個孩子	this is the wurzel chimpanzee .
之後每五年或每六年她只生一仔這麼長的童年期內小猩猩很有依賴性 , 需要照料晚上和媽媽一起睡 , 騎在她背上	and then every five years or six years , she gives birth to a very long childhood , and the chimpanzees are dependent on her back , taking care of the night with her mom , riding on her back .
我們認為這麼長的童年期對黑猩猩很重要 , 這牽涉到學習 , 就像童年之於我們一樣	we think this longterm childhood is so important to chimpanzees , and it involves learning , like our childhood .
在各種不同形態動物的進化過程中由於大腦變得日益複雜我們發現 , 在一種個體的生命歷程中學習的作用日益重要	in the process of evolution in various forms of animals , because the brain is becoming increasingly complex , we've found that learning is increasingly important in an individual's lifespan .
年紀小的黑猩猩花很長時間觀察它們的長輩做什麼	young chimpanzees spend a lot of time watching what their elders do .
我們現在知道 , 他們能模仿所見的行為表現	we now know that they can mimic how they behave .
我們認為正是由此從那些在非洲研究的所有不同黑猩猩種群身上看到的使用工具的不同行為這些行為是怎樣透過觀察、模仿和實踐從一代傳到另一代的所以 , 我們可以把這些使用工具的行為說成是原始文化	and we think it's the way that we think of all the different toolusing behaviors that we've seen in africa , from different chimpanzee populations , through observations , imitation and practices , from one generation to another , so we can think of these toolusing behaviors as primordial cultures .
黑猩猩沒有語言 , 我們以前提到過	chimpanzees don't have language . we talked about it before .
但他們確實有一整套非常豐富的姿態和動作其中許多與我們的很像 , 甚至一模一樣並且具有相同涵義黑猩猩打招呼時會擁抱	but they do have a very rich set of gestures and motions , many of which are very similar to ours , even identical , and embrace when it comes to chimpanzees who are hello .
他們也親吻、牽手、一個拍另一個的背	they also kiss , hold hands , pat one on the other .
他們也虛張聲勢地恐嚇 , 或者仍石頭	they're also terrifying , and they're still rocky .
在黑猩猩的社會里 , 我們發現很多很多憐憫、示愛以及真正利他的例子	in chimpanzee societies , we found a lot of compassion , love and real examples .
和我們一樣 , 不幸的是 , 他們也有天性中陰暗的一面	unfortunately , like us , they have the dark sides of their nature .
他們可以極度兇殘 , 甚至像一種原始戰爭	they can be incredibly brutal , even like a primordial war .
多數情況下 , 這些極具攻擊性的行為是直接針對相鄰社群中個體的	in most cases , these extremely aggressive behaviors are directly targeted to individuals in adjacent communities .
這些攻擊大多是為了爭奪地盤	most of these attacks are for geography .
我覺得 , 與別的生物相比黑猩猩更有助於我們認識到 , 人類和動物王國裡的其他成員終歸併無明顯界限	i think it's even helpful to realize that humans and other members in the kingdom of animals end up remaining inexplicable .
這種界限非常模糊 , 並且隨著我們更多的觀察會一直更加模糊下去	it's a very fuzzy boundary , and as we get more observations , we keep getting more fuzzy .
我1960年開始的研究一直持續到現在	my research started in 1960 , and it's been going on .
這些黑猩猩在野生環境過著複雜的社會生活最重要的是 , 他們幫助我們認識到 , 我們與形形色色的動物在地球上共處 , 我們是其中一部分不能與這些動物分割開來	the chimpanzees have a complicated social life in the wildlife environment , and most importantly , they help us realize that we live with animals that live with us on this planet , and we're partly unable to separate ourselves from these animals .
所以 , 發現黑猩猩和世界上其他眾多生物一樣失去聚居地 , 是很讓人難過的	so it's sad to find that chimpanzees , like so many other creatures in the world , are losing habitats .
這只是一張從空中拍的照片你可以看到森林覆蓋的gombe高地	this is just a photograph from the air , and you can see the gombe highlands covered in the forest .
16年前 , 我走遍整個地區意識到在公園之外 , 這片森林在1960年時沿著tanganyika湖東岸綿延不絕小巧的、面積只有30平方英里的gombe國家公園就坐落在這裡那時一個問題進入我腦海	16 years ago , i traveled all over the region , and i realized that outside the park , this forest stretched along the east coast of lake tanganyika , along the east coast of lake tanganyika , with only 30 square miles of gombe national park .
" 我們怎麼能進而去試圖拯救這些出了名的黑猩猩 , 而住在國家公園周圍的人卻在為生存而掙扎 ? "	" how can we get there trying to save these famous chimpanzees , and people who live around the national park are struggling to survive ? "
那裡人口眾多 , 非單薄的土地所能承受	there's a lot of people , not just thin land .
隨著來自蒲隆地的難民湧入來自剛果的人跨湖過來 , 住在那裡的人數增加著	as refugees from burundi flooded in from congo crossing lakes , the number of people living there was increasing .
那些人非常窮無力從別的地方買吃的	those people are very , very poor to buy from other places .
一個計劃由此產生 , 我們稱之為 " 關愛 "	and that's when a project arose , which we call love .
它用整體化的方式來改善住在湖周圍村子裡的人的生活	it's a generalized approach to improving the lives of people living in the villages around the lake .
剛開始是小規模的 , 有12個村子 。 現在是24個	at first it's small , it's 12 villages .
這裡沒有時間去深入介紹 , 不過該計劃包括象林木苗圃等事情 , 以及適於在山上這片目前嚴重剝蝕幾近沙漠的土地上耕種的方法	there's no time to go into this , but this project includes raised beds in elephant shins , and it's appropriate to this mountain that's currently pretty eroding landscape approaching deserts .
控制、防止土地侵蝕的方法	control , prevent land from erosion .
收回過度使用的農田的方法以便兩年內這些農田可以重新有收成	overused farming can be recycled in just two years , and these farms can be recycled .
幫助村民從井裡取得淡水	help villagers get fresh water from the well .
或許建一些校舍	maybe you build some schoolrooms .
我認為最重要的是與小規模群體婦女合作給她們提供微型信用貸款的機會	i think most importantly , working with smallscale groups of women and giving them opportunities for microcredit loans .
全世界的情況一樣 , 在所有貸款中我們收回了大約95%	all over the world , we recycled about 95 percent of all loans .
使婦女能夠受教育後工作給女孩子提供獎學金 , 以便讓她們完成中學學業很清楚 , 世界各地婦女的教育程度提高了 , 家庭人口數目就會下降	it allows women to be educated to give scholarships to girls , so they can finish high school , and it's clear that women are educated everywhere in the world , and families are going down .
我們提供計劃生育和艾滋病及其病毒方面的資訊	we provide information on reproductive and hiv and their viruses .
這項計劃實施之後自然保護方面發生了一些事情	and then something happened on natural protection .
自然保護方面發生的事情是 , 住在這24個村子裡的農民並沒有把我們看成是跑來研究整個一夥兒猴子的一夥兒白人順便說一下 , 現在很多工作人員是坦尚尼亞人而當我們開始 " 關愛 " 計劃時進入村子的是一個坦尚尼亞小組	what's happening to natural protection is that the farmers who live in these 24 villages did not look at us as one bunch of monkeys who studied the whole bunch of monkeys , by the way , a lot of them now are tanzanians , and when we started the village with love , it was a tanzanian team .
和村民交談的是一個坦尚尼亞小組詢問村民對什麼感興趣	i talked to the villagers as a tanzanian group and asked the villagers what interests them .
他們對自然保護感興趣嗎 ? 一點也不	are they interested in nature conservation ?
他們對健康感興趣 , 他們對教育感興趣	they're interested in health . they're interested in education .
隨著時間推移 , 隨著他們境況開始改善他們開始不斷理解更多有關自然保護的必要性	over time , as their circumstances began to improve , they began to understand more about the need for natural protection .
他們開始理解當山上較高位置的數被砍光以後可怕的土地侵蝕和泥流就來了	they began to understand that when the higher numbers on the mountain were cut off , the horrible land eroded and mud streams came .
現在 , 我們正在開發所說的大gombe生態系統	now , we're developing what we call the biggmbe ecosystem .
這是一片國家公園以外的地區綿延包括了所有這些各種各樣剝蝕了的土地	this is an area outside the national park that's extended , including all these different lands that have eroded .
由於這些村子生活標準高一些他們實際上同意把他們土地的10-20%放到高地一側以便當樹長回來時黑猩猩會再次擁有綠色走廊它們可以藉此穿行以便這是他們基因繁殖所必需的與國家公園外其它殘餘群體互動	and because these villages have a higher standard of living , they actually agree to put 10 to 20 percent of their land on the high ground so that when the trees come back , the chimpanzees will have green corridors , and they'll be able to wear them so that this is the kind of necessary necesary for their gene breeding to interact with the rest of the community outside of the national park .
所以 " 關愛 " 計劃成功了	so caring worked .
我們在非洲其它地區複製這項計劃在其它面臨極端人口壓力的荒野之地	we replicated this program in other parts of africa in other parts of the wilderness of extreme population pressure .
但是 , 就像我們在ted開始的所有這幾天一直討論的非洲的問題是主要問題	but , like all of the problems that we've been talking about here at ted over the last few days , it's a major problem .
那裡非常貧窮	it's very poor .
有大量的人生活在不那麼肥沃的土地上尤其當你把樹砍倒使得土壤裸露 , 任風侵蝕同時處於絕望的人砍倒越來越多的樹以便為他們自己和家人努力培育糧食這樣會發生什麼 ? 有些東西會開始犧牲讓步	there's a lot of people living on less fertile land , especially when you cut down the trees and erosion the soil , and wind erosion , and those who are in despair are increasingly cutting down more and more trees for themselves and their families , and what's going to happen is , some things will start to sacrifice them .
還有別的問題不僅在非洲而且是其它所有發展中世界 , 甚至是地球上所有地方我們在對我們的地球做什麼呢 ?	and other questions not only in africa , but all the developing world , or anywhere else on earth , what are we doing to our planet ?
著名科學家 , e.o.威爾遜說過 , 如果地球上每個人的生活標準都達到歐美平均水平我們就再需要三個地球	e . o . wilson , the famous scientist , said that if everybody on this planet had a standard of living , the average american standard , we would need three more .
今天他們說是四個 。 可我們沒那些個 , 我們只有一個	today they say four . but we don't have those . we only have one .
發生了什麼 ? 我是說 , 這裡的問題是 , 我們在這裡或許可稱為地球上有史以來最有智慧的生命有著非凡的大腦能夠運用這些ted會議上闡述備至的這些技術但我們卻在毀壞著這個惟一的家園	what's going on here ? i mean , the question is , we might call it the most intelligent life on earth , and it's extraordinary to be able to apply these ted conferences to these extraordinary techniques , but we're destroying this one .
全球各地的原住民在做重要決定前都會坐到一起 , 然後問 " 這決定如何影響我們接下來的七代人 ? "	indigenous peoples around the world would sit together before important decisions , and ask , " how does this decision affect the next seven generations ? "
今天 , 重要決定我這裡不特別談非洲而是發達世界牽涉幾百萬美元以及以及幾百萬人的重要決定卻只是問 " 這會如何影響下次股東大會 ? "	today , important decisions i'm not here to talk about africa , but about the industrial world , about millions of dollars and millions of people's most important decisions , are just saying , " how does this affect the next shareholder meeting ? "
這些決定卻影響非洲	these decisions affect africa .
當我開始遊歷非洲談論黑猩猩面臨的問題及其日益消逝的森林我愈來愈意識到如此之多的非洲問題是如何與以前的殖民開發有關的	and as i started traveling around africa talking about the problems that chimpanzees face and the forest that they were fading , i became more and more aware of how africa was related to its former colonial development .
因此我開始在非洲之外旅行 , 在歐洲演講在美國演講 , 去亞洲	so i started traveling outside africa , talking in europe , talking in the united states , going to asia .
每一地都有這些糟糕的問題	everywhere there's these terrible problems .
你知道我說的是什麼問題 , 這包括汙染問題	you know what i'm talking about , including pollution .
我們呼吸的空氣經常毒害我們	the air that we breathe constantly poison us .
泥土毒害我們的食物	mud poisoning our food .
水水也許是本世紀我們要面對的最要緊問題之一每一地 , 水都被農業、工業、家用化學制品所汙染全世界都還在噴這些製品似乎沒辦法從過去的經驗獲利	water may be one of the most important problems we faced this century , and everywhere , water is being polluted by agriculture , industries , homeschool chemicals , and the world is still spraying , and these products seem to be unable to profit from the past .
紅樹被砍倒海嘯等影響日益加重	redwoods are being cut down , tsunami , and so on .
我們談過土壤侵蝕	we talked about soil erosion .
我們不計後果地燒過化石燃料連同其它所謂溫室氣體導致了氣候變化	we have burned fossil fuels regularly , along with other things called greenhouse gases , causing climate change .
終於 , 全世界的人都開始相信有什麼事發生了 , 我們的氣候不對勁兒了	and finally , all over the world , people are believing in what's going on , and something's wrong with our climate .
全球氣候互相牽連	global climate is interconnected .
最受不利影響的是窮人	the worst impact on the poor is the poor .
已經受影響的是非洲	africa has been affected .
在次撒哈拉非洲的許多地區 , 乾旱非常嚴重	in many parts of subsaharan africa , droughts are very , very serious .
雨終於下起來時 , 又常常導致洪水及更多的不幸 , 貧窮、飢餓和疾病週而復始	when the rain finally rises , it often leads to floods and more , and unfortunately , poverty , hunger and disease all over again .
還有很多人住在土地供養不起的地區太窮 , 買不起食物因為全部土地都剝蝕了 , 所以也沒法離開	and there's a lot of people living in land that's incredible to feed , that can't afford to buy food , because all the land is eroded , so there's no way to go .
於是有了沙漠化一點點漫延 , 漫延 , 漫延同時最後的樹也被砍倒	so with desertification , a little bit of desertification , a little bit of delay , and a little bit of delay , and at the same time , the last tree
這種事情不光在非洲遍佈全球	this is not just happening all over the world .
所以我不覺得奇怪當我在世界各地旅行時碰到那麼多年輕人 , 他們看上去失去了希望	so i don't think it's surprising that when i travel around the world , there are so many young people who seem to have lost hope .
我們似乎已經失去了智慧 , 那種屬於原住民的智慧	we seem to have lost wisdom , the wisdom of indigenous peoples .
我想問 , 這是為什麼 ?	and i wanted to ask , why is this ?
你們覺得在這異常聰明的大腦ted技術作為例證的那種大腦和人的心臟之間會有某種隔絕嗎 ? 用非科學的術語來談談根據愛和同情 。 有隔絕嗎 ?	do you think there's an isolation between the brain and the human heart , that's not scientifically based on love and compassion ?
這些年輕人 , 當我和他們講話時基本上他們要麼情緒低落 , 要麼無動於衷或者痛苦、憤怒他們或多或少說的是同一件事情 " 我們這麼感覺是因為我們覺得你們損害了我們的未來 , 並且我們對此無能為力 。 "	these young people , when i'm talking to them , are basically emotionally low , either imprecise or painful or angry they're talking more or less about the same thing , " we feel like it's because we feel like we've damaged our future and we can't do anything about it . "
我們確實已經毀壞了他們的未來	we've certainly destroyed their future .
我有三個小孫子 , 每次看著他們我就想 , 從我像他們那麼大以來 , 我們是如何損害這個美麗的地球的我感覺到這種絕望	i have three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them , i think , how we've damaged this beautiful earth , and i feel that sense of despair .
我們由此開展這項我們稱之為 " 根與芽 " 的計劃恰好始於這裡 , 坦尚尼亞現在已經傳播到世界上97個國家	and so we started this project called roots and shoots , which is where tanzania has now spread to 97 countries around the world .
專案的名字是具有象徵意義的根造就堅實的基礎	the name of the project is the symbolic root of the meaning .
芽看上去細小 , 在陽光照耀下卻可穿破磚牆	shoots look tiny , and under sunlight , they can break through brick walls .
磚可以看成是我們給地球造成的環境的和社會的問題這是希望的訊息	bricks are viewed as the environmental and social issues we have created on earth , and that's a message of hope .
世界各地成千上萬的年輕人可以取得突破 , 為了所有生物 , 讓這個世界更美好	hundreds of thousands of young people around the world have been able to get a breakthrough , for all living things , to make the world a better place .
" 根與芽 " 的最重要訊息每一天 , 我們每一個人都在改變世界	the most important message of roots and shoots , each and every day , each of us is changing the world .
我們有一個選擇這屋子裡我們每一個人我們都有一個選擇 , 關於我們想做些什麼來改變世界	we have an option for each and every one of us in this room , and we all have a choice about what we want to do to change the world .
很窮的人沒有選擇我們要改變這些事以便窮人也有選擇	very poor people have no option . we have to change those things so that poor people have choices .
" 根與芽 " 小組都選三個方案	the roots and shoots groups choose three programs .
取決於成員年齡 , 所在國家在城市還是鄉下 , 來選不同的方案	it depends on member age , in the country , in the cities , in the country , in the country , in the rural area , to choose a different solution .
基本上 , 我們現在的計劃從學前一直到大學愈來愈多的成人開始建立他們自己的 " 根與芽 " 小組	basically , we're planning right now from school to college , more adults are starting to build their own roots and shoots groups .
每個小組在彼此之間選擇三種不同的方案 , 來創造更加美好的世界承認所有這些不同問題是互相聯絡彼此影響的	each group chooses three different programs to create a better world acknowledging that all these different problems are interconnected to each other .
因此他們的方案之一將會幫助他們自己的人類社群	so one of their programs is going to help them have their own human community .
然後 , 如果他們能幹 , 他們可以籌集資金幫助世界上其它地區的社群	and if they can do that , they can raise funds to help communities in other parts of the world .
他們的方案之一將會幫助動物不光是野生動物也包括家養動物	one of their programs is going to help the animals , not just the wildlife , including the families .
他們的方案之一將會幫助我們共處的環境	one of their programs is going to help us live together .
交織在所有這些方案中的訊息是學著與我們自己、家庭、社群和諧相處 , 包括國家之間 , 不同文化之間不同宗教信仰之間 , 以及我們和自然世界之間	the message in all these programs is to learn to harmonize ourselves , families , communities , between states , between cultures , between religious beliefs and between us and the natural world .
我們需要自然世界我們不能繼續象現在這樣破壞世界了	we need the natural world , and we cannot continue to destroy it now .
我們只有一個地球	we only have one planet .
就在非洲這裡 , 僅僅選出一個或兩個 " 根與芽 " 小組正在實施的方案只要一個或兩個方案在坦尚尼亞、烏干達、肯亞、南非、剛果、布拉扎維、獅子山、喀麥隆以及別的團體 。 就象我說的 , 遍佈世界97個國家	just here in africa , just one or two roots and shoots groups are implementing in one or two programs in tanzania , uganda , kenya , south africa , congo , congo , sierra leone , cameroon and other groups .
當然 , 他們種樹 , 他們種有機蔬菜	of course , they plant trees . they grow organic vegetables .
他們在難民營養小雞賣雞蛋得些微薄收入或只是把雞蛋給家人吃並覺得自豪和獲得權力因為他們自己種植蔬菜養殖小雞就不再無助 , 不再依賴他人	they sell eggs tiny in refugee camps , or just feed eggs to their families and feel proud and empowered because they grow their own chickens no longer depend on others .
這個方案在烏干達實施了給予前童軍一些心理上的幫助	this program implemented some psychological help in uganda .
實施這些方案讓他們重塑自我	implementing these programs reinvents themselves .
再一次 , 他們成為社會上的有用一員	once again , they become useful in society .
我們也在監獄實施該計劃	we also implemented it in prisons .
所以現在沒時間實施更多的 " 根與芽 " 計劃	so there's no time for more roots and shoots .
哦 , 他們也致力於艾滋病及其病毒方面的工作	oh , they're also working on aids and their viruses .
那是 " 根與芽 " 計劃非常重要的組成部分由大孩子跟小孩子談話	it's a very important component of roots and shoots , and it's partly adults talking to kids .
還有無意懷孕及類似事情年輕人更願意聽別的孩子的 , 而不是成人的	there's unintended pregnancy and things like young people who are more willing to listen to other children than adults .
希望 。 我周遊世界被問及的就是這個問題 " 珍 , 你見過這麼多可怕的事情 , 你看著你的黑猩猩數量在減少 , 從世紀之交的大約一百萬到現在的不足15萬 。 那麼多其它動物也一樣	hope . the question that i've been asked around the world is this: " jane , you've seen so many terrible things , you're looking at the decline in your chimpanzee population from about a million to 150 , 000 animals .
森林消失 , 過去是森林的地方變成沙漠	the forest disappears , where it used to be a desert .
你真的有希望 ? " 嗯 , 有 。	do you really have hope ? " " well , yes .
你不可能來參加象ted這樣的會議 , 卻不報希望 , 對吧 ?	you can't come to a ted conference like this , but you don't wish , right ?
當然 , 有希望 。 希望之一是這令人稱奇的人腦	of course , there is hope . one of the hopes is this amazing human brain .
我是說 , 想一想技術	i mean , think about technology .
我最後還是很激動 , 碰到人們談論堆肥廁所	i ended up getting excited when people talk about composting toilets .
這是我愛討論的話題之一	this is one of my favorite topics .
我們就把所有這些水衝下馬桶 , 這很可怕	and we just sprinted all this water down the toilet . it was horrible .
然後談論了可再生能源 , 非常重要	and then talk about renewable energy , very important .
我們為孩子關心過地球嗎 ?	have we cared about the planet for our children ?
我們多少人有孩子或者孫子、侄子、外甥 ?	how many of us have children or grandchildren , nieces , nephews ?
我們關心他們的未來嗎 ?	do we care about their future ?
如果關心他們的未來 , 作為全球精英我們可以做些事情 。 我們可以做決定 , 每天怎樣生活	if we care about their future , as global elites , we can do things .

我們需要切斷一次性使用塑膠和一次性塑膠的源頭 , 使得它們在全球範圍內每天不會再進入大海 。	we need to cut the sources of plastic and oneoff plastic so that they don't enter the ocean every day in the world .

我和其他的一群人們都關注這個塑膠汙染問題 , 組建了塑膠汙染聯盟 。	i and a bunch of other people looked at this plastic pollution problem and created the plastic pollution alliance .

在美國 , 塑膠垃圾回收率少於百分之七 。	in the united states , plastic garbage is less than seven percent .
大家想實際看看 , 特別當塑膠變成塑膠瓶 , 絕大多數塑膠瓶僅被降級回收 , 或者焚燒 , 或運到中國 。	people want to see , especially when plastic becomes a plastic bottle , most of the plastic bottles are just being recycled or burned or shipped to china .
當一個塑膠瓶可以被重製成一個塑膠瓶 , 或者重被使用時 , 正是被降級回收 , 使得塑膠瓶被製成小塑膠體 , 使得一個塑膠瓶不再被製成塑膠瓶回收利用 。	when a plastic bottle can be recreated into a plastic bottle , or reused , it's being recycled so that a plastic bottle can be made into small plastic bottles so that a plastic bottle can no longer be recycled .
對我們而言 , 這是個重大問題 。	it's a big problem for us .
我們關注 , 並讓人們思考的另一件事是我們在原本3個r原則前 , reduce、reuse、recycle , 加了第四個r原則 , 它就是拒絕使用 。	one of the things that we're paying attention to and letting people think about is that , before we had three rr principles , reduce , recycle , plus the fourth rr principle , it was rejection use .
無論何時 , 拒絕使用一次性使用塑膠和即丟塑膠 。	whenever , refuse to use oneoff plastic and disposable plastic .
有替代品的使用 。 其中一些是非常老套 。	there are alternatives . some of them are very old .
我自己現在收集這些很酷的耐熱玻璃容器 , 使用這些而替換高興派和特百惠派塑膠容器來儲存食物 。	i'm now collecting these cool , tourist glass vessels using these to replace privilege privilege pupils and trafficient plastic containers
我知道我這樣做有利於我自己和我的家庭 。	i know that i do it for myself and for my family .
我們選擇使用不鏽鋼瓶和玻璃瓶是很容易的 , 你如果要出門 , 記得帶不鏽鋼瓶 , 讓它灌滿水 , 或者濾過水 , 而不要購買塑膠瓶裝水 。	it's easy to use stainless steel bottles and glass bottles , and if you want to go , remember rusty steel bottles , fill it up , or filter it water , instead of buying plastic bottles .
我猜我想要告訴大家的是我知道你們大家關於此塑膠汙染知道得很多漂在大海上的塑膠是個嚴重的問題 , 但這是我們做為消費者自身產生的問題 , 我們也能自身解決這問題 。	i guess what i'd like to tell you is that i know that many of you know about this plastic pollution is a serious problem in the ocean , but it's a problem that we're generating as a consumer , and we can solve it ourselves .
我們透過提高這問題的意識 , 教導人們選擇可替換性產品 , 能夠解決這問題 。	we're teaching people to choose alternative products by raising the awareness of this problem .
所以無論何時 , 請選擇使用可替換性產品 , 拒絕使用一次性使用塑膠和即丟塑膠 。	so whenever you want to use replaceable products , refuse to use oneoff plastic and disposable plastic .
我們可以切斷源頭 , 阻止這塑膠汙染到我們的海洋裡 , 透過如上4r行動 , 拯救我們的海洋 , 拯救我們的家園 , 拯救我們自己 。	we can cut the source and block this plastic pollution into our oceans by saving our oceans , by 4ring , by saving our homes , by saving ourselves .

所以說 , 我們並沒有一個便捷的渠道去獲取這些資訊 , 這些能幫助我們做出應該要幹什麼的最佳決定的資訊 。	so we don't have a quick channel to get this information that helps us make the best decisions we have to make .
因此 , 我的實驗室的研發團隊完成了一系列的發明 , 在不改變使用者行為的條件下 , 幫助使用者快速簡單的獲取這些資訊 。	so my lab's r&amp ; d team completed a series of innovations to help user access this information without changing the user's behavior .
現在 , 我將這個裝置展示給大家 。 這是我們至今最成功的版本 , 仍然在不斷改進 。	now , i'm showing this to you . this is the most successful version of us ever , and it's still improving .
我現在正佩戴著我們其實是把市面上常見的一些元件組裝在了一起 。 順便提一下 , 目前這個裝置的成本是350美元 。	now i'm wearing something that we actually assembled common components on the market .
我佩戴著一個相機 , 就是一個簡單的網路攝像頭 , 一個便攜的用電池供電的投影儀和一個小鏡子 。	i'm wearing a camera , a simple webcam , a portable battery projector and a little mirror .
這些元件跟我口袋中的手機進行通訊 , 手機作為一個通訊和計算的裝置 。	these components communicate with my phone in my pocket as a communications and computational device .
畫面中 , 是我的天才學生pranavmistry , 他設計並製造了這整套系統 。	this is my genius student pranavistry , who designed and built this entire system .
我們可以看到 , 當他靠近任何表面時 , 資訊就會被投影到表面上 , 他就用雙手來進行操作 。	and we can see that when he approaches any surface , the information gets projected on the surface , and he operates with his hands .
系統會跟蹤四個主要的手指 。	the system tracks four major fingers .
在這裡 , 你可以看到他戴著用於標示的指套 。	and here , you can see him wearing advice that he's used for .
如果你想要更美觀 , 可以把你的指甲染成不同的顏色 。	if you want to be more beautiful , you can infect your nails into different colors .
攝像頭會跟蹤這四個手指 , 識別他的任何手勢 , 例如 , 他可以開啟longbeach的地圖 , 進行放大或者縮小等等操作 。	the camera is tracking these four fingers , identifying any gestures in his hands , for instance , and he can open up a map of longbeach to magnify or shrink or operate .
這個系統也能識別 " 象徵性手勢 " , 比如 , 當你做出這個 " 拍照手勢 " , 系統就會拍照 , 把你面前的東西拍下來 。	this system also recognizes symbolic gestures , such as when you make this photograph gesture , the system takes a picture and takes a picture of what is in front of you .
當他回到medialab實驗室之後 , 他可以走近任何一面牆 , 投影出他拍的所有照片 , 用各種自然手勢 , 進行整理 , 歸類 , 改變大小等各種操作 。 所有操作都用手勢來完成 。	when he got back to the medalia ab lab , he could walk up to any wall and project all the photographs he had taken using various natural gestures , organize them , categorize them , change things , change things , all gestures .
你們當中有些人兩年前在這裡應該看過jeffhan演示微軟的surface系統 , 你們可能覺得:這套系統跟surface看起來很像 。	some of you may have seen jeff han playing a microsoft surface system two years ago , which you may think is very similar to surface .
沒錯 , 這兩套系統都是用自然手勢 , 用雙手來操作 。	well , both of these systems are natural hand gestures , using both hands .
但區別是 , 我這套系統可以在任何表面上操作 , 你可以走近任何表面 , 如果沒有可用的表面 , 你還可以用自己的手與投影的資料進行互動 。	but the difference is , i can use this system to operate on any surface , and you can go to any surface , and if it doesn't work , you can interact with your own hand and projection data .

所以如果你和不健康的人在一起隨時間推移會受到很大影響 。	so if you're together with unhealthy people , it's going to be a huge impact .
如果你朋友娛樂的主意是體力活動 , 打保齡球或打曲棍球腳踏車或園藝工作 , 他們飲酒適量飲食適度 , 他們投入工作值得信任 , 最後就會對你產生最大影響 。	if your friend's entertainment is the idea of physical activity , playing bowling or playing hockey bikes or gardening , they drink adequately for diet , they invest trustworthy jobs , and they end up having the biggest impact on you .
食物沒有什麼用 , 歷史上沒有一種食物能養活2%的人口 。	there's nothing to use for food , there's no food in history that feeds two percent of the population .
練習專案通常在一月開始十月結束 。	practice projects often end in january .
至於長壽 , 沒有藥片或其他什麼東西能在短期內奏效 。	as for longevity , there's no pill or anything that can be done in the short term .
但當你想到你的朋友是長期的冒險活動時 , 因此 , 它是你為增加壽命和讓生命生機勃勃能夠做的最重要的事情謝謝	but when you think about your friends as the longterm adventures , therefore , it's the most important thing you can do to increase your lifespan and keep life alive .
能導電的墨水、一<unk>開關就由透明變不透明的窗戶、能播放音樂的果凍--這些東西確實存在 。 catarinamota說:現在是時候嘗試他們了 。 mota將帶領我們認識這些新穎和神奇的材料 , 她說 , 弄清楚這些材料的神奇之處的最好方式就是用它們來做實驗 , 不斷嘗試並樂在其中 。	the ink that conducts electricity , the comfort of it , the transparent windows , the frozen frozen that play music , actually exists . catari mota says it's time to try them now . mota will take us to understand these novel and magical materials , and she says , the best way to make sense of these materials is to try and experiment with them and try and experiment with them .
creativity , design , technology	it's ivity , it's serious .
catarinamota:玩轉智慧材料	catarina mota: play with smart materials .
我有一位葡萄牙朋友 , 其祖父用一輛腳踏車和一臺洗衣機改裝成一輛汽車供家人乘用 。	i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather used a bicycle and a washing machine to convert it into a car for multiplication .
他這樣做 , 一是因為他買不起車 , 但更重要的是因為他知道如何改裝汽車 。	he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but more importantly because he knew how to modify it .
曾經 , 我們都懂得一些機械的工作原理 , 也知道它們是怎麼製造出來的 , 所以我們能夠自己製作和維修它們.或者至少基於我們的瞭解作出明智的購買決定 。	at one point , we've all understood some mechanical work principles and know how they were made , so we can make and fix them ourselves , or at least based on our understanding of making smart purchases .
但我們很多這些diy的實用性技能在20世紀的下半葉就流失了 。	but a lot of these diy practical skills were lost in the lower part of the 20th century .
但是現在 , 製作者社群和開放資源模式正在把這些物品的工作原理和製造材料的知識帶回到我們的生活中 。 而且我相信我們需要把這些知識帶到下一個層面 , 也就是了解構成這些物品的元件 。	but now , the maker community and the open source model is bringing the principles and the knowledge of the objects back to our lives , and i believe we need to take that knowledge to the next level , the components that understand these things .
我們很多人都知道 , 像紙和織物這樣的傳統材料是什麼做成的 , 以及它們是如何生產的 。	many of us know what traditional materials like paper and fabrics are made of , and how they're made of .
但是現在我們有了一些令人驚歎的未來複合材料-如可以變形的塑膠、可以導電的油漆、可以變色的顏料和可以發光的織物 。	but now we have some amazing future composite materials such as deformable plastics , conductive paint , transformable pigments and glowing fabrics .
下面讓我們來看一些新材料 。	so let's look at some new materials .
這種導電墨水可讓我們 , 拋棄傳統的印刷電路板或電線的方法而直接用導電墨水來畫電路板 。	this conductive ink allows us to throw away traditional printed circuit boards or wires and draw circuit boards directly .
比如我手裡拿著的這個小裝置 , 是我們用導電墨水做成一個觸控性的感測器 , 一旦接觸人的皮膚 , 這個小燈就會亮起 。	so this little device that i'm holding in my hand is we're using conductive ink to make a touch sensor , and once it's in contact with the skin , this little light light will light up .
導電墨水已經被藝術家們應用到創作中了 , 最新的進展表明我們很快就能把它應用在鐳射印表機和鐳射筆中.	conductive ink has been applied to the artists , and the latest progress has been shown that we can apply it to a laser printer and a laser laser .
這是一張泡浸過無色光漫顆粒丙烯酸的紙.	this is a piece of paper that was bathed in colorless comic books .
只浸過普通丙烯酸的紙只在其邊緣周圍有漫光現象 , 而這張浸過無色光漫顆粒丙烯酸的紙 , 當我們開燈時漫光會照亮整張紙.	there's only a phenomenon that's bathed in normal acrylic acid , and this is a phenomenon that's surrounding it , and this is bathed with colorless odds of acrylanine , and as we drive the light , the light will light up the entire paper .
就目前所知 , 這種材料已經被應用到室內設計和多點觸控系統兩個領域中了 。	as far as we know , this material has been used indoor design and multiple touch systems .
而熱變色顏料在特定的溫度下會改變顏色 。	and thermal pigments change color at certain temperatures .
我先把這張東西放到一個電熱板上溫度設定比外界溫度稍高一點然後你可以看到發生了什麼.	i'm going to put this thing on a board that's a little bit hotter than the outside world , and you can see what's going on .
除了其它用途 , 這種材料主要用作嬰兒奶瓶的製造 。 它能告訴你什麼時候瓶裡的東西涼到可飲用的溫度 。	in addition to other uses , this material is primarily used for baby bottles , and it tells you when things are cold and drinkable .
這些就是我們通常所說的 " 智慧材料 " 的幾個例子 。	these are a few examples of what we usually call smart materials .
幾年內 , 它們將被應用到很多我們日常使用的物件和科技產品上 。	in a few years , they're going to be applied to a lot of the objects and technological products that we use every day .
我們也許還不會有科幻小說向我們保證的飛行汽車 , 但是我們能擁有隨溫度變色的牆 , 可以捲起來的鍵盤 , 和一<unk>開關就變不透明的窗戶 。	we may not yet have science fiction flying vehicles to our guarantee , but we can have walls that change temperature , keyboards that can curl up , and light , shimming opaque windows .
我是科班出身的社會科學家 , 為什麼今天我在這裡講智慧材料 ?	i'm a social scientist from the kuban , and why am i talking about smart materials today ?
首先 , 我是個製造者 。	first of all , i'm a maker .
我對於東西如何運轉和怎樣製作有好奇心 , 我也相信我們應該對我們這個世界的組成材料有更深的瞭解 , 並且現在 , 我們對於這些構成我們未來的高科技材料瞭解不多 。	i'm curious about how things work and how they make things , and i also believe that we should know much more about the materials that make up our world , and we don't know much about these hightech materials that make up our future .
要獲得少量的智慧材料是很難的 。	it's hard to get a small amount of smart material .
有關如何使用這些材料的資訊也很少 , 它們是如何製作的資訊就更加少得可憐 。	there's very little information about how to use these materials , and there's less information about how to make them .
目前 , 它們絕大多數都存在於貿易機密和專利中 , 只有大學和大公司才能得到 。	currently , most of them are in trade secrets and patents , only universities and big companies can achieve them .
所以三年多以前 , 我和kirstyboyle發起了一個叫做openmaterials的專案 。	so more than three years ago , i started a project called open maternals with kirstyboyle .
在那個網站上 , 我們和想要加入我們的任何人 , 分享實驗 , 釋出資訊 , 鼓勵其他人為此作出力所能及的貢獻 , 並且收集像研究論文和像我們一樣的製造者所製作的教程一類的資源 。	on that website , we share experiments with anyone who wants to join us , release information , encourage others to make a contribution to this , and collect resources like research papers made by producers like us .
我們希望把這一網站做成一個大規模的、集體生成的資料庫 , 蒐集用智慧材料diy的資訊 。	we want to make this website a database of massive , collectively produced data collections that are using smart materials diy .
但是我們為什麼要關心智慧材料是如何工作和它們是用什麼來製造的呢 ?	but why should we care about how smart materials work and what they're made of ?
首先 , 因為我們無法影響我們不理解的東西 , 我們不理解和不會用的東西還會反過來影響我們 。	first of all , because we can't influence things that we don't understand , things that we don't understand and don't use are affecting us .
我們使用的東西 , 我們穿的衣服 , 我們住的房子 , 都對我們的行為、健康和生活質量上產生深遠的影響 。	the things we use , the clothes we we wear , the house we live in , have a profound impact on our behavior , our health and our quality of life .
所以如果我們將要生活在一個由智慧材料構成的世界中 , 我們就應該知道並瞭解它們 。	so if we're going to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .
第二 , 同樣重要地 , 創新總是來源於修補匠 。	secondly , just as importantly , innovation always comes from fixers .
很多時候 , 是業餘愛好者而非專家 , 發明和改進了諸如山地車、半導體、個人電腦、甚至飛機 。	oftentimes , amateurs instead of experts , inventions and improvements like mountain vehicles , semiconductors , personal computers , even airplanes .
材料科學的最大挑戰是它的複雜性 , 以及對昂貴的儀器的需求 。	the biggest challenge of material science is the complexity and the need for expensive instruments .
但事實並非總如此 。	but that's not always the case .
伊利諾伊大學的兩名科學家在他們發表一篇關於用更簡便的方法制作導電墨水的論文時就明白了這個道理 。	two scientists at the university of illinois published a paper on making conductive inks easier .
jordanbunker在這一實驗之前是一個沒有任何化學經驗的人 。 他讀了這篇論文後在他的工作間裡用現成的物質和工具重複了這個實驗 。	jordan bonker was a person who didn't have any chemistry experience before this experiment , and he read this paper and repeated it with the existing materials and tools in his workshop .
他用了一個烤箱 , 而且他甚至在另一個科學家/製造者的教程的基礎上自制了旋渦混合器 。	he used an oven , and he even organized a vortex mixer on the basis of another scientist/maker’s teaching .
後來 , jordan在網上發表了他的實驗結果 , 包括所有他試過的沒成功的東西 , 這樣其他人可以學習然後複製這一實驗 。	later , jordan published his experiments online , including all the unsuccessful things he tried so that others could learn and replicate this experiment .
所以jordan主要創新方式是拿一個在設施齊全的大學實驗室裡創造的實驗 , 然後在芝加哥的一個車庫裡用便宜材料和自制的工具來重複實驗 。	so jordan's main innovation was to take an experiment that was created at the university laboratory and repeat it in a garage in chicago using cheap materials and autonomous tools .
在他發表的實驗結果基礎上 , 其他人可以接著做下去並且設計甚至更簡單的步驟和改進實驗 。	on the basis of the results that he published , others can then do and design even simpler steps and improvement experiments .
我想分享的另外一個例子她專案的目標是在突出材料富有表現力的特質的同時專注於製造者的創造力和製造技巧 。	another example i want to share with you is that her project targets to highlight the quality of materials while focusing on the creativity and the manufacturing skills of makers .
電子工具在教我們東西如何運轉這方面非常有力 , 但是它們設計中傳承下來的約束影響我們學習的方式 。	the electrical tools are very powerful in teaching us how things work , but the restrictions that they've inherited in their designs have influenced the way we learn .
所以hannah的方法 , 在另一方面 , 就是創制一系列的技術 , 來創造非常規的東西 , 透過教給我們材料本身的知識 , 把我們從事先設計好的約束中解放出來 。	so hannah's method , on the other hand , is to create a series of techniques to create very regulated things , to free us from the constraints that we've been preemptively designed .
在hannah眾多令人欽佩的試驗中 , 這個是我的最愛之一 。	this is one of my favorite experiments in hannah's many admirable experiments .
[ " 會說話的紙 " ]我們在這裡看到的只不過是一張紙上面的銅帶連線著一個mp3播放器和一塊磁鐵 。	[ " speech paper " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of copper connected to a piece of paper with an mp3 player and a magnet .
在麻省理工學院教授marcelocoelho研究的基礎上 , hannah使用各種材料創造了一系列紙質揚聲器 。 從普通的銅帶到導電的織物和墨水 ,	on the basis of marcelocoelho research at mit , hannah used various materials to create a series of paper speakers , from ordinary copper to conductive fabrics and inks .
就像jordan和其他很多製造者一樣 , hannah發表了她的配方並且允許任何人來重複這些實驗 。	like jordan , like so many other makers , hannah released her recipe and allowed anyone to come and repeat these experiments .
但是紙上電子是材料科學中最有前景的分支之一 , 因為它讓我們能創造出便宜又靈活的電子產品 。	but electronics on paper is one of the most promising branches of material science , because it allows us to create cheap , flexible electronics .
所以hannah的手工作品 , 和她分享了她的發現這個事實 , 打開了一扇門 , 通向兼具美學和創新的一系列新的可能 。	so hannah's handwork , she shared her discovery with her , opened a door to a new array of possibilities for both aesthetic and innovation .
製造者的有趣之處在於我們創造是出於熱情和好奇 , 並且我們不害怕失敗 。	what's interesting about makers is that we create passion and curiosity and we're not afraid to fail .
我們通常從非傳統的角度處理問題 , 並且 , 在這個過程中 , 最終發現其他方案或者更好的方法 。	we often deal with problems from an unconventional perspective , and in the process , we end up discovering other alternatives or better ways .
所以當更多的人願意用新材料做試驗的時候 , 更多的研究者就會願意分享他們的研究成果 ; 有更多的製造商分享他們的知識 , 我們就會有更好的機會來創造造福我們所有人的科技 。	so when more people are willing to do experiments with new materials , more researchers will be willing to share their work ; more manufacturers will share their knowledge , and we will have a better chance to create technology that benefits all of us .
我的感覺有一點像tednelson在70年代初期的感覺一樣 , 他寫道 , " 你們現在必需懂電腦 。 "	i felt a little bit like tednelson in the early '70s , and he wrote , " you need to understand computers now . "
那個時候 , 電腦是這些只有科學家關心的大型機 , 沒有人會夢想到放一臺在家裡 。	at that time , computers were these big opportunities that scientists cared about , and nobody would dream of putting in a home .
所以我今天站在這裡說 " 你們現在必需懂智慧材料 " 有一點奇怪 。	so i'm standing here today saying , " you need to understand smart materials a little bit strange .
請記住對於新興科技擁有先發制人的知識是確保我們在對未來的創造中有發言權的最好方式 。	keep in mind that primary knowledge of emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a voice in the creation of the future .
當我們開車是 , 我們就坐進了一個玻璃氣泡中 , 鎖上門 , 踩下油門 , 依靠眼睛為我們自己導航 。 即使我們僅僅只能看見車前車後的幾輛車 。 但是假如汽車能互換關於位置、速度的資料 , 並運用預測模型來為每一位司機測算最安全的線路呢 ? 詹妮佛海麗構想了一個零車禍的世界 。	when we drive the car , we sit in a glass bubble , lock the door , step down the gas gate and navigate ourselves , even though we only see a few cars behind the car , but if the car exchange information about position , speed and use models to predict the safest route to measure each one of the drivers ?
詹妮弗海麗:汽車若能交流車禍或可避免	jennifer halley: cars can communicate accidents or inevitably .
讓我們來面對一樁事實吧開車是一件危險的事	let's face it: driving is a dangerous thing .
它是我們不願意去想的事物之一但事實上那些神像和平安符世界各地都有人把它們擺在儀表盤的上方這就無意中透露出一個我們都心知肚明的事實	it's one of the things that we don't want to think about , but in fact , those divine and peaceful meetings around the world are putting them on top of the dashboard , which inadvertently reveals a fact that we all know .
車禍是死亡的主因尤其在美國16到19歲的美國人群中死亡的主因並且百分之七十五的車禍都與毒品和酒精無關	car accidents are the cause of death , especially in the united states between the ages of 16 and 19 , and 75 percent of all car accidents have nothing to do with drugs and alcohol .
沒人能給出確切答案但我記得我第一次出車禍	no one could give the exact answer , but i remember the first time i got in a car accident .
我當時還是個開車的新手 , 當時正在外面高速路上開著車 。 我突然看見我前面汽車的剎車燈亮了	i was a new driver , and i was driving outside on the highway , and all of a sudden i saw the brake light in front of me .
我當時想好吧他減速了那我也減速好了	and i thought , okay , he's slowing down , and i'm slowing down .
我踩了剎車	i stepped on the brakes .
但是我前面那個人並不是在減速	but the person in front of me wasn't slowing down .
他停車了突然停車在高速路上突然停車	he stopped and suddenly stopped on the highway , and suddenly he stopped car
速度從65邁瞬降到0	from 65 to 0 .
我猛踩剎車	i slammed on the brakes .
我當時感覺到我的車的防抱死系統啟動了但車還在行駛並沒停下來的意思我也知道我的車停不了了安全氣囊也鼓了起來車報廢了但幸運的是沒有人受傷	i felt that my car's hugging system was starting , but the car was still driving and didn't stop , and i knew that my car stopped , and the airbags were getting rid of it , and fortunately nobody was injured .
但我根本不知道我前面那輛車要停而且我想我們可以比那做得更好	but i didn't even know that the car was going to stop in front of me , and i thought we could do better than that .
我想我們透過實現 " 讓汽車之間對話 " 來改變我們的駕駛體驗	i think we can change our driver's experience by making car conversation .
我希望你們能思考片刻思考一下現在的駕駛體驗是怎麼樣的	i want you to think about what the experience of driving is like for a moment .
坐進車裡關上車門你就已經置身在一個玻璃氣泡中	you're sitting in your car and closed the door , and you're already in a glass bubble .
你不能直接感受到你周圍的世界	you can't just feel the world around you .
因為你坐在車這樣一個不小的空間裡	because you're sitting in a space like this .
你的任務就是導航你只能看見道路的一部分並且以超人類的速度行駛在其他的 " 金屬巨人 " 間	your task is to navigate , and you can only see the road , and drive at superhuman speeds , at other metal giants .
對吧 ? 你只能靠雙眼來導航	right ? you can navigate by your eyes .
對你別無他法眼睛並非是用來幹著活兒的但是有些事情你就必須得做 , 比方說 , 你想換個車道那你第一件要做的事是什麼	there's no other way for you to do it , but there's something that you have to do , like , you want to change lanes , and what you do the first thing you do .
將眼睛從車道上移開對	remove the eyes from the driveway .
將目光從你前進的方向移開轉彎檢查一下盲點然後就一直開根本不注意自己在往哪裡開	turn your eyes from the direction you're moving , check the blind spot , and keep track of where you're heading .
所有人都這麼做這是安全的駕駛方式	all of us do that , and that's a safe way to drive .
我們為什麼這麼做 ? 因為我們別無選擇我們必須作出一個抉擇是朝這兒看還是朝那兒看	why do we do this ? because we have no other choice .

我們並不想對我們學生也這麼做 。	we don't want to do that to our students .
所以我們有機會可以真正開啟教育 。	so we have the opportunity to really open education .

所以我們開始了進行細胞探索的一個計劃 , 這將展示分子細胞生物學中內在的真和美由此學生會有更全面的印像能把所有事情聯絡在一起	so we're starting a program called cellular exploration , which will show the truth and beauty in molecular cellular biology , where students will have a more holistic impression , where they can connect everything together .

而這些微型機器卻是生命的中心 。	and these micromachines are at the center of life .

同時賦予我們心智 。	it gives us minds .

我們想出了一個劇情大綱 , 那就是 , 巨噬細胞正在流過一個毛細血管它們不時接觸著毛細血管管壁它們收集來自細胞散佈在毛細血管管壁上的訊號 , 這個訊號是:在外側 , 有炎症發生 , 巨噬細胞本來是無從得知 。	we came up with a plot , which is , the macrophages are flowing through a hairy blood vessel and they're touching the capillary walls all the time they're collecting signals from the cells spreading across the walls of the capillary capillary vessels , which is , outside , inflammation happens , and the macrophages are unknown .

事實上 , 沒有這些機器的話 , chris , 今天的出席狀況將非常慘烈 。	in fact , without these machines , chris , attendance today is going to be very terrible .
這是細胞中fedex快遞人員:	this is the fedex director in the cell .
這個小傢伙叫驅動蛋白他拉著一大袋新合成的蛋白質 , 到細胞所需要的任何地方--不論它是細胞膜 , 還是一個細胞器也不管是用來搭建什麼 , 還是修復什麼	this little guy is driving the protein , and he's pulling a bag of newly synthetic proteins , anywhere in the cell whether it's a membrane , whether it's a cell , whether it's a cellular device , whether it's for building something or repairing something .
我們體內每個細胞 , 大約有10萬個這樣的小傢伙此時此刻 , 正在跑來跑去而我們大約有100萬億個細胞 。	we have about 100 , 000 of these little guys in our bodies right now , running around , and we have about 10 trillion cells .
所以無論你覺得自己有多懶本質上 , 你並不是什麼都沒做 。	so no matter how lazy you feel , you don't do anything .

貝基布蘭頓計劃在一年裡就在他的小貨車裡住並且遊歷全國 , 但是當沮喪加劇而且自由作家的工作泡湯的時候 , 他的旅營就變成了無家可歸了 。 在這個溫馨的演講中 , 她描述了她作為美國無家可歸的工作者之一的獨特經歷 。	baki brandon was planning to live and travel throughout the country for a year , but when depression and free writers worked bubble soup , his travel camp became homeless , and in this gentle talk she described her as a homeless worker in america .
adventure , happiness , life , personalgrowth , poverty , socialchange , society , storytelling	" adventure , " " happiness , " " of course , " of course , " of course , " of course , " of course , of " poverty , " of course , " of the mind , of course , " of the story .
貝基布蘭頓:我無家可歸的一年	brendy brandon: one year i was homeless .
我是一個作家 , 一個新聞記者 , 我也是一位具有強烈求知慾的人 。 所以在做新聞記者的22年裡 , 我知道了很多新奇的事物 。	i'm a writer , i'm a journalist , i'm also a very strongly cognitive person , so for 22 years of doing journalists , i know a lot about novelty .
而三年前 , 我學會做的一件事就是變成隱形人 。	and one of the things i learned three years ago was that i became invisible .
我成了一個無家可歸的工作者 。	i became a homeless worker .
我辭掉了報紙編輯的工作在我父親那年二月去世之後我決定去旅行	i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died that february , and i decided to travel .
他的去世對我打擊非常大 。	his death hit me very big .
當時這麼做 , 是因為有很多我想去感知和處理的事 。	and this was because there were so many things that i wanted to perceive and deal with .
旅遊時我天天都在露營 。 並且決定在休旅車裡住一年就當作是一段長期野營旅行 。	i was traveling every day , camping and deciding to live in the suv for a year as a longterm camp trip .
所以 , 我就帶上我的貓 , 我的羅特威爾犬和露營的裝備裝載到1975產的雪佛萊旅遊車上 , 開車去看日落但當時完全沒想過三件嚴重的事	so i took my cat , my rotwellerdog and camping equipment , loaded onto the 1975 chevley ride , drove to the sunset , but i hadn't thought about three serious things .
一:社會將住房即使是很小的房間 , 和人的價值等同起來 。	one: social housing is equal to human worth .
二:我沒有意識到其他人的負面言語對我們本身的影響是多麼嚴重 , 假如我們放任不管 。	two: i didn't realize the negative impact that other people had on us if we let go .
三:我沒有意識到無家可歸是一種生活態度而不是一種生活方式 。	three: i didn't realize homelessness is a lifestyle , not a lifestyle .
一開始 , 住在車裡是很不錯的 。	at first , living in a car was great .
我在露天洗澡 , 正常的去外面吃東西 。	i was taking a shower , normally eating outside .
而且有時間去抒發情感 。	and there's time for emotional expression .
但是後來 , 因我父親去世而帶來的悲憤和痛沮開始加劇 。	but then , the anger and the depression that my father died began to accelerate .
我自由作家的工作結束了 。 我就需要去找一件全職工作來支付我的賬單 。	my free author's work ended , and i needed to find a fulltime job to pay my bills .
從一個非常溫和的春天變到一個極其炎熱的夏天會怎樣呢 。	from a very gentle spring to an extremely hot summer .
不管車停在哪都是難以忍受的不用說也很明顯我帶著一隻貓和一隻狗 , 而且非常的熱 。	regardless of the car park is unbearable , obviously i'm carrying a cat and a dog and i'm very hot .
貓從車窗來回的跑 。	the cat runs back and forth from the window .
狗跑到了狗狗護理中心 。	the dog ran to the dog nurse center .
不管什麼時候 , 只要可以 , 我就會去用在辦公大樓和卡車車站裡員工用的淋浴 。	whenever i can , i go to showers for office buildings and truck stops .
或者在公共衛生間裡洗洗 。	or wash in public health .
在夜裡車裡的溫度很少會降到華氏80度以下 , 這使我幾乎無法入睡 。	at nighttime temperatures dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , which made me almost impossible to sleep .
食物在高溫下腐壞 。	food rotted in the heat .
冷藏櫃裡的冰幾個小時就化完了 , 非常苦悶的時期 。	the ice in the refrigeratory locker was completed , very painful time .
我沒錢找公寓 , 或者找不到讓我可以養狗和貓的地方 。	i had no money to find an apartment , or to find a place where i could raise dogs and cats .
我不想把它們拋棄 。 所以我繼續待在旅行車裡 。	i didn't want to throw them away . so i stayed in the van .
但炎熱的天氣使我飽受折磨以至於在夜裡走50英尺到車外面的公共衛生間都懶的動 。 我用桶和垃圾袋當廁所 。	but the hot weather made me so afflicted that i was walking 50 feet into the middle of the night to the outside of the vehicle , lazy for the public health packets and garbage bags .
當冬天來臨的時候 , 溫度驟降到零度以下 。 然後就一直這麼冷 。	when the winter came , the temperature dropped below zero degrees , and it stayed that cold .
我又遇到了一堆新問題 ,	and i had a bunch of new questions .
每晚我的車都停在不同的地方 。 這樣才可以不讓警察發現以至於和警察爭吵 。	every night , my car parked in different places so that it wouldn't let the police find the police to argue with the police .
當然 , 並不是每次都成功 。	of course , not always successful .
但是 , 我覺得我已無力掌控自己的生活了 。	but i felt like i had no control over my life .
我也不知道什麼時候或者是如何發生的 , 我這麼快就從一個有才的寫手 , 新聞從業者變成一個無家可歸 , 住在車裡的女人這簡直是快的難以置信 。	i didn't know when or how it happened so quickly , i went from being a talented writer to being an homeless woman living in a car , incredibly fast .
我並沒有變 。 我的智商沒有降低 。	i didn't change . my iq did not decrease .
我的才能 , 我的正直 , 我的價值 , 所有關於我的這些東西都還是一樣 。	my talent , my integrity , my worth , everything about me is still the same .
但是從某種程度上 , 我還是改變了 ,	but in a way , i changed .
我越來越沮喪 , 像一個漩渦一樣不斷地往下沉 。	i was increasingly frustrated , sinking down like a swirl eddy .
後來有人介紹我去一個專為無家可歸之人開的健康診所 。	and then someone introduced me to a health clinic that was prescribed for homelessness .
我去了 。 我有三天都沒有洗澡了 ,	i went . i didn't bathe for three days .
我和其他那些排隊的人一樣沮喪 , 身上的味道也很難聞 。	i was as depressed as anybody else in line , and i was very difficult to smell .
我只是沒有喝醉或者興奮 。	i just wasn't drunk or excited .
當一些無家可歸的人意識到 , 包括一個以前在大學任教的教授 , 他們說: " 你不是無家可歸 , 你真正在這裡的原因是什麼 ? "	when some homeless people realized , including a professor who used to teach at university , they said , " you're not homeless , what's the reason you're really here ? "
其他的無家可歸的人不把我當作是無家可歸的人看待 。 但是我自己是這麼認為的 。	other homeless people don't see me as homeless people , but i do .
後來 , 教授聽了我的故事後他說 , " 你有工作 , 有希望 。	and then , after the professor listened to my story , he said , " you have work , you have hope .
真正無家可歸的人並沒有希望可言 。 "	there is no hope for a real homeless person . "
診所針對我沮喪開的藥物的副作用讓我有點自殺的傾向 。 我還記得當時想 , " 如果我自殺了 , 可能沒人會發現的 "	the doctor's side effects that i was a little bit of a suicide tendency for the side effects that i was depressed about , and i remember thinking , " if i'm suicidal , no one's going to find it . "
在那不久後 , 我的一個朋友就告訴我 , 她聽說提姆路塞特 , 一個全國知名的記者在全國播放的電視節目上談論到了我 。	not long after that , a friend of mine told me about tim luther , a nationally renowned journalist talking about me on national television .
一篇我寫的關於我父親的短文 , 在他去世前一年寫的 , 被收錄到了提姆的新書裡 。	an essay i wrote about my father , a year before he died , was received in tim's new book .
他那時在做巡迴演講 , 提到我的寫作 。	he was giving a tour to mention my writing .
當我發現提姆路塞特 , 前meetthepress節目的調解員 , 在談論我的寫作 。 而我卻生活在停在沃爾瑪停車場裡的旅行車裡面 , 我開始笑了 ,	when i found tim luther , former meetthepress , talking about my writing , and i was living in a van that parked in walmart parking lot , i started laughing .
我開始笑 , 因為這正是問題根結 , 我是一位作家呢 , 還是一位無家可歸的女人 ?	and i started laughing , because that's the root of the problem , am i a writer , or is it a homeless woman ?
於是我走進一家書店 。 找到提姆的書 。	so i went into a bookstore . i found tim's book .
我站在那 , 又重新讀了一遍我寫的短文 。	and i stood there , and i reread the text that i've written .
因為我是一位作家 ,	because i'm a writer .
是一位作家 。	it's a writer .
在那之後 , 我很快就搬回了田納西 。	since then , i quickly moved back to tennessee .
有時住在車裡 , 有時會去朋友家睡沙發 。	sometimes living in a car , sometimes going to a friend's house to sleep on the couch .
我又重新開始寫作了 。	i started writing again .
在接踵而來的夏天裡 , 我又成為了一名新聞記者 。	in the aftermath summer , i became a journalist .
我得了獎 , 住在我自己的公寓裡 。	i got a prize , and i lived in my own apartment .
我不再無家可歸 。	i was no longer homeless .
我也不再被無視 。	i was no longer blind .
無數的人在從事著全職和兼職的工作 , 而且住在他們的車裡 。	countless people are engaged in fulltime jobs and parttime jobs and living in their cars .
但是社會還繼續汙衊他們並視住在交通工具裡或者睡在街上為犯罪 。	but society remains obstacles who live in the transportation vehicles or sleep on the streets for crime .
所以那些無家可歸 , 有工作但是無家可歸的人 , 大部分還是隱藏著的 。	so the homeless , the working but homeless , most of them are still hidden .
但是如果你見到了 , 僱用他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 並給予他們希望 。	but if you see them , hire them , encourage them and give them hope .
只要有希望 , 人類的精神可以克服一切困難 。	with hope , human spirit can overcome everything .

我們需要讓足夠的婦女擁有權力並且培養男人心中的婦女力量	we need to have enough women own power and cultivate women's strength in men .
這裡當然是指年輕男人了	and this is , of course , young men .
老男人們都沒求了 , 只能等著他們死光	the old man didn't get it , so he could just wait for them to die .

不過若是可以選擇 , 我寧願擁有勇敢的心像旺加里.馬塔伊 , 蘇曼麗.馬恩 , 珍妮和羅斯.馬培德那樣的	but if i had a choice , i would rather have a brave heart like wangari maathai , somali marian , jennie and rose mabed .

不僅僅是消極地等待改變 , 而是參與改變	not just negatively , waiting for change , but getting involved in change .
為什麼不這樣 ? 這是能夠做得到的 。 看看這裡 , 充滿了知識 , 活力 , 才華和科技	why not ? it's possible . look here , it's full of knowledge , dynamic , talent and technology .
讓我們走出冷氣房 , 捲起袖子開始行動 , 帶著我們的熱情創造一個近乎完美的世界	let's get out of the cold room , roll up our sleeves , start to act , and take our passions to create an almost perfect world .
在一個倫敦那麼大的城市裡 , 每天都要消耗掉三千萬噸糧食 。 但是 , 這些食物都從何而來 ? 建築師carolynsteel探討每天餵養一個城市的神話 , 介紹古代的食物運輸如何影響城市的形成和發展 。	in a city that's that big in london , it costs 30 million tons of food every day , but where does all this come from , and the architect carolynsteel looks at the myth of feeding a city every day , introducing how food transportation impacts the formation and development of the city .
cities , culture , food , globalissues	audience: adam , global issues .
carolynsteel:食物如何塑造我們的城市	carolyn steel: how food shapes our cities .
如何餵養一個城市 ?	how do you feed a city ?
這是我們這個時代的一個重大問題之一 。	this is one of the big problems of our time .
然而很少人會問這個問題 。	and very few people ask this question .
我們習以為常了 , 我們走進商店的時候走進餐廳的時候 , 或是一個小時後我們進入這個劇院的門廳總會有食物等著我們它們很神奇地從某個地方冒出來	we used to walk into the restaurant when we walked into the store , or an hour later , we entered theater's doorway , there was always food , waiting for us , and magically emerged somewhere .
然而 , 當你想像每一天 , 在一個倫敦那麼大的城市 , 要生產足夠的食物運輸、交易這些食物 , 烹飪 , 食用 , 最後扔棄它們而且類似的事情每天都發生著在地球上的每一個城市都如此每個城市都有食物供應 , 這件事很不可思議	however , if you imagine that every day in a city that was the size of london produced enough food transportation , trading these foods , cooking , cooking , eating , finally throwing them away , and things like that happen every day , every day , every city on this planet , so it's amazing .
我們住在每天有食物供應的城市 , 彷彿這是世界上最自然的事情 , 我們忘記了我們也是動物 , 所以我們需要進食 , 事實上我們要依賴自然界就如同我們的祖先要依賴自然界一樣 。	we live in a city that has food supply every day , as if it's the most natural thing in the world , and we forgot that we are animals , so we need to eat , and in fact we depend on nature as our ancestors depend on nature .
隨著我們越來越多人到城市生活 , 越來越多的自然界正在變成我身後的這些特別的景象這是巴西matagrosso的大豆田用來種食物養活我們	as more and more of us go to urban life , more and more natural worlds are becoming these special visions behind me , this is a soybean field for brazilmatagrosso in order to grow our food .
這些特別的景象我們很少人親眼目睹過	these particular images , few of us have ever seen them .
越來越多的這些地貌不只是生產食物養活我們	more and more of these landscapes are not just producing food to feed us .
隨著我們越來越多人移居城市越來越多人吃肉所以每年全球有三分之一的糧食現在是用來餵動物而不是餵養我們人類	as more and more of us move to cities , more and more people eat meat , so that a third of the world's food is now feeding animals rather than feeding us humans every year .
雖然說需要3倍的糧食事實上卻是10倍的食物來餵養一個人 , 如果從餵養動物的糧食也計算在內這並不是一個很有效率的餵養方式	and while it takes three times as much food , it's actually 10 times as much food to feed a person , and if you feed an animal , you know , it's not an efficient way of feeding an animal .
這是一個越來越重要的問題	it's an increasingly important question .
到2050年 , 預測有兩倍的人口將在城市居住	by 2050 , it's predicted that twice as many people will live in cities .
預測到也將需要兩倍的肉和奶類製品的消耗	it's predicted that it's going to take twice as much meat and milk to produce it .
所以肉的消耗和城市化是共同發展的	so meat consumption and urbanization are coevolving .
這就將引發一個很重大的問題	and that leads to a really big problem .
要餵養60億的飢餓人口在2050年	to feed six billion hunger people in 2050 .
這是個大問題.如果我們還像我們現在這麼發展 , 我們很可能沒法在2050年解決這個問題	it's a big problem . if we're still here , we're probably not going to solve this problem by 2050 .
每年有1900萬公頃的雨林消失它們用作開墾新的耕地	every year , 19 million hectares of rainforest disappear , and they use it to cultivate new arable land .
儘管與此同時我們也失去等量的現有耕地 , 因為鹽鹼化或水土流失	and at the same time , we're losing an equal amount of arable land because of saltification or soil .
我們也急需化石燃料	we really need fossil fuels .
在歐洲 , 我們需要10卡路里的能量來生產1卡路里為我們消耗的食物	in europe , we need 10 calories of energy to produce one calories of food that we consume .
儘管這些食物我們都是花了很多功夫才生產出來事實上我們卻不珍惜它們	although these foods are a lot of hard work to produce , we actually don't value them .
在美國有一半食物被扔棄	half of the food is discarded in the united states .
最終 , 在這漫長過程的最後我們將沒法養活我們這個地球	ultimately , at the end of this long journey , we will not be feeding our planet .
我們中10億人肥胖 , 還有多於10億的人處於飢餓中	one billion of us are obese , and more than one billion people are hungry .
這些都沒有道理	none of this makes sense .
當你發現現在80%的全球食物貿易僅由五家跨國公司控制 , 這是挺可怕的	when you find out that 80 percent of the global food trade is controlled by five multinationals , it's pretty horrible .
隨著我們搬進城市 , 世界正在接受西方的飲食	as we move into cities , the world is accepting western diet .
如果我們展望未來這不是個可持續的飲食方式	if we look at the future , it's not a sustainable way of eating .
我們怎麼會走到這一步 ?	how did we get here ?
更重要的是 , 我們應該怎麼做 ?	and more importantly , what should we do ?
先回答那個較簡單的問題 , 首先我想說 , 在大概1萬年前是這個過程的開始在古代的中東地區也就是廣大的新月狀的地區	well , the simpler question , first of all , is that it started about 10 , 000 years ago in the middle east , which is an ancient new monthly region .
因為你可以看到它是新月形的	because you can see it's a new month .
同時它也是廣大的	it's also enormous .
就在這裡 , 大概1萬年前2大偉大的發明農業和城市化在此發生幾乎在同時 , 同一地點	right here , about 10 , 000 years ago , 20 great inventions of agriculture and urbanization happened almost at the same time , at the same time .
這並不是偶然因為農業和城市是緊密聯絡的.它們需要彼此	it's not accidentally because agriculture and cities are intimately connected , and they need each other .
因為糧食的發現我們的遠古祖先 , 第一次第一次生產出足夠的糧食並且產量穩地 , 這幫助他們長期居住下來	the discovery of food was that our distant ancestors , for the first time , produce enough food and yield steadily , helping them live longtermly .
如果我們看一下當時那些居住地我們可以看到他們是緊密的	if we look at those habitats back then , we can see they're tight .
他們被農田圍繞並由一些大的廟宇統領著例如這一個在烏爾的神殿事實上 , 他們是很有效的精神統領 , 食物分發中心 , 兩者結合	they were surrounded by farms and led by large temples like this one in ur , and in fact , they were effective psychological reigns , food distribution centers , combinations .
因為這些神殿組織耕作收集這些糧食 , 供奉給諸神然後把諸神沒吃的食物發還給人們	because these temple tissues are gathering these foods , serving them to the gods , and then giving them back the food that the gods don't eat .
所以這些城市的精神和物質生活都用糧食和收成掌控並維持城市的生活	so the spirit and the physical life of these cities is used to eat and to control and maintain urban lives .
事實上 , 過去的每個城市都是如此	in fact , every city in the past has done that .
當然 , 並不是每個都是那麼小的城市	and of course , not all cities are that small .
比如很著名的羅馬城有大約100萬居民在公元一世紀的之前	rome , which is famous , has about a million residents before the 1 . d .
那麼 , 這樣的城市是如何維持供給的呢 ?	so how does a city like this supply ?
在我眼裡 , 我把答案稱作 " 古老的城市之路 "	in my eyes , i call it the " ancient city road . "
基本上 , 羅馬有通往海洋的道路這樣使從很遠的地方進口食物成為可能	basically , rome has roads to the ocean , which makes it possible to import food from a very distant location .
這樣是在古代能實現的唯一的方法因為陸上運輸相當困難鑑於路況不好	this is the only way that ancients can achieve this , because transportation is very difficult because it doesn't work well .
而且食物的消耗是很快的	and food is fast .
所以羅馬常常發動戰爭攻打像迦太基和埃及那樣的國家僅僅是為了得到他們的糧食儲備	so rome regularly launched war attacks in countries like ghamaki and egypt just to get their food reserves .
其實 , 事實上 , 你可以把帝國的擴張理解為一種長期的軍事化的購物狂歡	in fact , you can understand the expansion of the empire as a kind of longterm militarization of shopping .
事實上 , 我喜歡這個事實 。 我不得不指出的是羅馬在一個時期 。 我認為這非常特別	in fact , i love that fact . i have to argue that rome was at one time . i think that's very special .
所以羅馬形成自己的海岸線根據他的口味	so rome formed its own coastline , based on his taste .
但是還有一件有趣的事情發生在前工業化的世界	but there's an interesting thing that's happening in the preindustrialized world .
如果我們看看十七世紀倫敦的地圖我們可以看見作物從泰晤士河畔出產的位於地圖的底部	if we look at the maps of london in the 17th century , we can see crops coming out of the banks of the thames river , at the bottom of the map .
因為市場在城市的南部	because the market is in the south .
道路從那裡通向主要消費市場戚普塞街這裡也是糧食的主要消費市場	the roads went from there to mainstream consumer , relatives purse street , which is also the main consumer market for food .
如果我們隨便看看這裡的一條街道的名字bread街 , 你可以明白三百年前這裡都發生了什麼	if we look at one of the streets in this room , bread street , you can see what happened 300 years ago .
這個道理同樣使用於魚類	it's also used in fish .
魚當然是從河裡面打撈出來的	fish , of course , came out of the river .
billlingsgate是倫敦有名的賣魚市場在1980年之前	billynsgate was a famous selling fish market in london before 1980 .
這是很特別的 , 真的 , 當你仔細想想	it's very special , really , when you think about it .
每個人都在這裡遊蕩拿著像轉頭一樣的大哥大還有 , 在港口還有發臭的魚	everybody's wandering around with the big brother of rotation and the port and the stinky fish .
這是在城市中關於食物的另一件事情一旦一種食物在某個城市站穩腳跟它的地位很難被動搖	this is another thing about food in the city , and once a food is stabilized in a certain city , it's very difficult to shake it .
肉是一個非常不同的故事了因為 , 動物自己走向城市	meat is a very different story , because animals go to cities .
因此 , 倫敦消費的大量肉類是從西北方過來的從蘇格蘭和威爾士	so , a lot of meat consumption in london is coming from the northwest , from scotland and wales .
當他們過來 , 抵達城市的西北方這就說明了為什麼smithfield倫敦一個非常有名的肉類市場 , 在這裡產生	when they came , they reached the northwest of the city , which illustrates why smithfield london was a very famous meat market .
家禽從anglia的東部來 , 去往東北部	domestic avians come from the east of ananglia to the northeast .
我感覺這有點像一個天氣播報員然後鳥兒都飛過來了它們的腳被小帆布鞋包裹著	i felt like a weather announcer , and the birds flew over , and their feet were wrapped around by little canvas .
然後當它們在東部降落的時候具體說來是在戚普塞街 , 也就是它們被賣掉的地方這也就是戚普塞街被稱為 " 家禽 " 街的原因	and when they landed in the east , they specifically ended up in the relatives purse street , where they were sold , which is why the relatives purse street was called domestic bird street .
事實上 , 如果你看看任何一個城市的地圖在工業化時代之前你能夠發現食物是如何進入城市的	in fact , if you look at any map of any city before industrialization , you can see how food goes into the city .
事實上 , 你可以看出食物是如何塑造一個城市的透過閱讀街道的名稱 , 你就會發現很多線索	in fact , you can see how food shapes a city by reading the names of the streets , and you can see a lot of clues .
星期五街 , 在過去的日子中是一個在星期五買魚的地方	friday street , in the past , was a place to buy fish on friday .
但是 , 你同時也必須想象那裡到處都是食物	but you also have to think about food everywhere .
因為街道和公共區域是食物買賣的唯一地點	because the streets and the public areas are the only places that food buys .
如果你想象一下1830年的smithfield你會發現很難在這樣一個城市裡面生活下去並且不留意食物的來源	if you think about smithfield in 1830 , it's very difficult to live in a city like this and not pay attention to the source of food .
事實上 , 當你在星期日吃午飯的時候你將很有可能聽到窗外的牛羊的叫聲在三年以前	in fact , when you're eating lunch on sunday , you're very likely to hear the call from the cow outside the window three years ago .
因此 , 顯然他是一個有機城市屬於有機迴圈中的一個部分	so , apparently , he's part of an organic city that's part of an organic loop .
但是 , 10年後 , 一切都改變了	but then 10 years later , everything changed .
這是大西鐵路在1840的照片	this is a photograph of the great western railway in 1840 .
你可以看見 , 一些早期的鐵路乘客們是豬和羊群	you can see some early railroad passengers pigs and sheep .
一夕之間 , 這些動物不再走進市場	all of a sudden , these animals stopped walking into the market .
他們被屠宰了在鄉村的某個地方	they've been slaughtered somewhere in the countryside .
然後他們透過鐵路來到了城市	and they came to the city through railroads .
這些改變了一切	and that changes everything .
首先 , 他第一次使城市成長變成了可能不論地點、成為什麼規模和形狀的城市	first of all , he made cities grow , for the first time , no matter what the location , what the size and shape of the city is .
城市發展過去受到地理的限制城市需要透過很艱難的方式獲得食物	urban development used to be restricted by geography , and cities need to get food in a tough way .
突然 , 他們從地理限制中解放了出來	all of a sudden , they liberated from their geographic constraints .
你可以看看倫敦的地圖在鐵路建成後的90年它從容易餵飽的一小點透過動物步行到市場等方式成長成為大型的奢侈的大都市步行運輸再也不能餵飽每個人不論是對人還是對動物	you can see the map in london in the 90 years after the railroad was made , it went from one small dot that was easy to feed , and through animal walks to markets , it grew into a massive , luxurious metropolitan walk , and no longer feed everybody , whether it's right or animals .
當然 , 這僅僅是開始 。 當汽車代替了火車這真正標誌這個過程的結束	and of course , that's just the beginning . when the train substituted the train , it really ended .
這是城市的最終解放從自然的束縛中完全的解放了	this is the ultimate liberation of the city from the constraints of nature , completely liberated .
這樣型別的城市沒有了原來城市的味道亂糟糟的市容 , 當然也缺少了人因為沒有人想要在這麼大的一塊地方步行	this type of city doesn't have the smell of the original city , and it's also the lack of people , because nobody wants to walk in such a big place .
事實上 , 他們都開小汽車去購買食物了開車去郊外的超級市場買回來一週需要的食物然後考慮到底如何規劃這些食品	in fact , they drove all the cars to buy food , drove to the suburban supermarket and bought food that they needed for a week , and thought about how to plan these foods .
這時刻 , 食物和城市的關係 , 完全的改變了	at this point , food and cities have changed completely .
過去買食物是在市中心在城市的最核心地帶	it used to be buying food at the center of the city .
買賣食物曾經是一種社會性的活動 ,	buying food used to be a social activity .
我們原來還需要烹飪 , 現在我們只需要加水或者是一些雞蛋 , 當我們在做蛋糕或者其他東西的時候	we also needed to cook . now we just add water or some eggs , when we make cakes or something .
我們不會在去聞聞食物來確認它是否可以吃了	we're not going to smell food to make sure it's okay to eat .
我們只是閱讀包裝袋上的使用說明就好	we just read the packaging descriptions .
我們沒有發現食物的價值 , 我們也不信賴它	we don't have the value of discovering food , and we don't trust it .
我們甚至擔心它	we worry about it .
從體會它的價值變成浪費	from recognizing its value to wasting .
當今食品工業最最諷刺的是他們讓生活極致地便利卻也使得一切更為複雜	one of the ironiest things about the food industry today is that it makes it extremely convenient , but it makes it even more complicated .
因為可以自由的建立新城市但是他們卻疏遠了人可貴的聯絡也就是人與自然的聯絡	because they're free to build new cities , but they're alienated from the valuable contacts between people and nature .
同時 , 他們也讓我們依賴這個系統這個系統 , 在我們看來 , 是不可持續的	meanwhile , they also allowed us to rely on this system , which is unsustainable , in our opinion .
所以 , 我們應該做點什麼呢 ?	so what should we do ?
這不是一個新的問題	this is not a new problem .
500年前 , 湯馬斯摩爾曾經問過自己	five hundred years ago , thomas more asked himself .
這是他的書《烏托邦》的主旨	this is the essence of his book , " utopia . "
它是一個半獨立的城邦如果這麼說聽上去還比較熟悉的話一天的行走你會看見所有人農場都在瘋狂的種植或者在自己的後院種植蔬菜然後一起享用鄉鎮的共有食物 , 等等	it's a semiindependent city , and if that sounds more familiar , walking on a day , you'll see that all of the farms are growing in crazy , or growing vegetables in their own backyard , and then sharing together food in the town , and so on .
我認為你可能想要說食物是烏托邦維持秩序的基礎儘管摩爾從來沒有這麼構想	i think you might want to say that food is the basis of utopia maintaining order , although moore never had the idea .
這裡有一個很著名的烏托邦藍圖來自埃比尼澤•霍華德的 " 花園城市 "	here's a very famous utopian blueprint from " garden city . "
