如果你想了解更多 , 給你的虛擬旅途畫上句號只需要讀讀書後的這些段落 。	if you want to learn more about virtual journeys , all you have to do is read these paragraphs .
非常感謝 。	thank you very much .
mit研究人員斯凱拉•蒂比茨從事自我裝配的研究一個取代建造東西的主意 , 我們能創建制作自己的材料 , 很像dna鏈打包的方式 。 目前還是一個巨大概念的早期階段 ; 蒂比茨向我們展示了三個還在實驗中的專案 , 我們可以一窺一個自我裝配的未來可能的樣子 。	the mit researcher , skeratibitz , who works selfassembling , is an idea that we can create materials that are very much like the dna link package , and we're still at the earliest stages of a giant concept ; tibiz shows us three programs in the experiment that we can glimpse into the future of selfassembly .
斯凱拉•蒂比茨:我們能製作可以製作自己的東西麼 ?	skera debitz: can we make things that we can make ourselves ?
今天我想向各位展示未來我們製作東西的方式 。	i want to show you today how we make things in the future .
我相信很快我們的建築和機器將能自我組裝 , 自我複製和自我修復 。	i believe soon our buildings and machines will selfassemble , selfreplicate and selfrepair .
因此我要向各位展示我所認為的製造業的當前狀況 , 接著再將其與一些自然系統比較 。	so i'm going to show you the current state of what i think of as manufacturing , and then compare it to some natural systems .
那麼在當前的製造業中 , 我們有摩天大樓兩年半的時間 , 50萬至上百萬個部分 , 非常複雜 , 使用了在鋼鐵 , 混凝土和玻璃方面的新技術 。	so in the current manufacturing industry , we have skyscrapers for two and a half years , 500 , 000 to million parts , very complex , using new technologies for concrete and glass .
我們有令人激動的機器 , 可以帶我們進入太空五年時間 , 兩百五十萬個部分 。	we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years , 2 . 5 million parts .
但另一方面 , 如果看看自然系統 , 我們有擁有兩百萬種類型的蛋白質 , 能在一萬納秒內摺疊起來 , 我們能在大約一小時內對帶有三十億鹼基對的dna進行復制 。	but on the other hand , if we look at the natural system , we have two million types of proteins that can fold up in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , we can reconstruct three billion base pairs of dna in about an hour .
這就是我們自然系統的複雜性 , 但它們非常高效 , 比我們建造的任何東西都要高效 , 比我們能建造的任何東西都要複雜 。	this is the complexity of our natural systems , but they're very efficient , much more efficient than anything we can build , much more complicated than anything we can build .
它們在能源方面更加高效 。	they're much more efficient in energy .
它們很少犯錯 。	they rarely make mistakes .
他們能自我修復保持長壽 。	they can selfrepair longevity .
關於自然系統有件超級有意思的事情 。	it's super interesting to talk about natural systems .
如果我們能將其轉換為我們的建築環境 , 那麼我們構建事物的方式就會有很大的潛力 。	if we can convert it into our architecture environment , then there's a great potential for how we construct things .
我認為關鍵是自我組裝 。	i think the key to selfassembly is selfassembly .
如果我們想要在自身的身體環境中利用自我組裝 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。	if we want to use selfassembly in our own environment , i think there are four key factors .
第一個是 , 我們需要解碼我們所要建造的東西的所有的複雜度也就是我們的建築和機器 。	the first is that we need to decode all the complexity that we want to build , our buildings and machines .
我們需要把它們解碼成簡單的序列基本上就是我們的建築運作的dna 。	we need to decode them into simple sequences that are basically the dna of how our buildings work .
接著我們需要可程式設計的部分這部分能接受這一序列並用於摺疊或是重塑 。	and then we need parts of programmable programmable parts that can accept the sequence and use folding or reimagining .
我們需要一些能量來進行啟用 , 使我們的這些部分能夠依照程式摺疊起來 。	we need some energy to start by folding these parts in the same program .
我們需要一些型別的糾錯冗餘以保證我們成功建造的就是我們想要的 。	we need some kind of error redundancy to guarantee that what we're successful at building is what we want .
因此 , 我要向各位展示一些我和我的同事正在進行的要實現這種自我組裝的未來的專案 。	so i'm going to show you some projects that my colleagues and i are working on to make this selfassembly future .
頭兩個專案是macrobot和decibot 。	the first two projects are macrobot and decibot .
這些專案都是大規模可重構機器人8英尺 , 12英尺長的蛋白質 。	these projects are all reconfigurable robots eight feet , 12 feet long protein .
它們嵌入機電裝置 , 感測器 。	they're embedded in electronics , sensors .
你需要把想要摺疊的方式解碼成 , 解碼成一系列角度負120度 , 負120度 , 0度 , 0度 , 120度 , 負120度 , 這類的東西 ; 一系列角度 , 或轉向 , 可以用電線把這個次序傳過去 。	you need to decode the way you want to fold it into a series of angles that are 120 degrees minus 120 , minus 120 degrees , zero degrees , minus 120 degrees , minus 120 degrees , a series of angles , or twists , and you can use wires to transmit this sequence .
每個單元獲取自己的訊息比如負120.它進行旋轉 , 檢查是否旋轉到位然後把序列傳給它的鄰居 。	each unit takes its own message like minus 120 . it rotates , checks if it spins to its neighbor .
有許多傑出的科學家 , 工程師 , 設計師為這個專案工作 。	there are a lot of brilliant scientists , engineers , designers who work on this project .
我認為這一專案真的揭示出:這真的可擴充套件麼 ?	and i think this project really reveals: is it really scalable ?
我是說 , 花費數千美元許多人時來製造這個八英尺的機器人 。	i mean , it cost thousands of dollars to build this eightfoot robot .
我們真的能擴大它麼 ? 我們真的能在每個部分中都嵌入機器人麼 ?	can we really expand it ? can we really embed robots in all parts ?
下一個問題是看看被動性 , 或被動地嘗試讓重組具有可程式設計性 。	the next problem is to look at passiveness , or passively try to make recombinations programmable .
但它更進了一步 , 它嘗試進行實際計算 。	but it goes even further , and it tries to do actual computation .
基本上嵌入了多數計算的基礎構建模組 , 數字邏輯閘 , 直接進入各個部分 。	basically embedded in most computational building blocks , digital gates , directly into each other .
這是與非門 。	it's not a gate .
每個要用於計算的門上都有一個四面體 , 有兩個輸入四面體 。	each of them has a tetrahedron on the door of computation , with two inputs .
其中一個是來自使用者的輸入 , 就像你在構建磚塊 。	one of them is the input from the user , just like you're building blocks .
另一個是來之前前放好的一塊磚的輸入 。	the other is a brick input that was previously introduced .
接著它會給出三維空間的輸出 。	and then it comes out to three dimensions of space .
這意味著使用者以他們想要的方式堆砌磚塊 。	it means that users build bricks in the way they want .
它依據之前所做的和你的指令進行計算 。	it calculates based on what you've done and what your commands have done .
現在它開始在三維空間內移動上或者下 。	now it starts moving up or down in three dimensions .
看左面 , [1 , 1]的輸入等於0輸出 , 表示向下 。	look at the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , and it goes down .
在右邊 , [0 , 0]的輸入是1輸出 , 表示向上 。	on the righthand side , [0 , 0] input is one output , expressing upward .
因此這真正的的意味是我們的結構中現在包含了我們想要構建的藍圖 。	so what this really means is that our structure now contains the blueprints that we want to construct .
因此關於想要構建的事物的資訊已經全部嵌入其中 。	so the information about what we want to construct has embedded in it all .
這意味著我們有了某種形式的自我複製 。	that means we have some form of selfreplication .
對這種情況 , 我稱之為自我導向複製 , 因為你的結構中包含了精確的藍圖 。	in this case , i call it selfdirect copying , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .
如果遇到錯誤 , 你可以替換一個部分 。	if there's a mistake , you can replace a part .
所有的本地資訊都嵌入其中 , 告訴你如何修復它 。	all local information is embedded in telling you how to repair it .
因此你有個可以攀爬的東西 , 能讀出它並一個一個的輸出 。	so you have something that can climb and read it and output one by one .
它是直接嵌入的 ; 沒有外部指令輸入 。	it's directly embedded ; there's no external input .
我要展示的最後一個專案名為偏心鏈條 , 它可能是我們現在看到的被動自我裝配系統中最令人激動的例子 。	the last project i'm going to show is called the paranoid chain , and it's probably one of the most exciting examples of passive selfassembly systems that we're seeing right now .
它具有可重構性和可程式設計性使它成了為了一個完全地被動系統 。	it has reconstructability and programmability that makes it so for an entirely passive system .
基本上就是你有了一連串的元素 。	basically you have a series of elements .
每個元素都是完全相同的 , 且它們是偏心的 。	each element is completely identical , and they are preferred .
每個鏈條 , 或每個元素想要向右轉或是向左轉 。	each chain , or every element wants to turn right or left .
如果你要裝配鏈條 , 需要為它程式設計 。	if you want to assemble the chain , you need to program it .
要告訴每個單元是要左轉還是右轉 。	tell each unit to turn left or right .
當你搖動這個鏈條時 , 它就摺疊起來程式設計你所為它編碼的任何結構因此這種情況下 , 一個螺旋體 , 火這種情況 , 兩個相連的立方體 。	and when you shake this chain , it folds up , and it programs whatever structure you code for it , so in this case , a spiral , fire , this situation , two cubes connected .
基本上你可以在三維空間內程式設計或是一維、二維這鏈條是完全被動的 。	basically , you can program this in three dimensions or onedimensional or twodimensional strands that are completely passive .
這向我們預示了怎樣的未來呢 ?	what's the future for us ?
我認為這告訴我們這些在我們的身體結構、我們的建築和機器中這種自我裝配、自我複製和自我修復的可能性 。	i think what this tells us is the possibility of selfassembly , selfreplication and selfrepairing in our bodies , our buildings and machines .
在這些部分中有新的可程式設計性 。	there's new programmability in those parts .
從中你能獲得計算的新可能性 。	there's a new possibility of computation .
我們將有空間計算 。	we will have spatial computing .
想象一下我們的建築、橋樑、機器 , 所有的磚塊都能進行實際計算 。	imagine our buildings , our bridges , our machines , all of these bricks can actually compute .
多麼令人驚奇的平行計算和分散式計算能力和新的設計可能性啊 。	what an amazing parallel computing and distributed computing power and new design possibilities .
這是項令人激動的潛力 。	it's an exciting potential .
我認為這些我向各位展示的專案僅僅是邁向未來的一小步 , 如果我們為一個新的自我組裝的世界實現了這些新技術的話 。	i think these projects i've shown you are just a tiny step towards the future , if we make these new technologies available to a new selfassembly world .
我們已踏上過月球 , 我們已測繪了大陸 , 我們甚至已去過海底最深處--兩次 。 還剩下什麼值得我們的下一代去探索 ? 生物學家和內森•沃爾夫提出了這樣的答案:幾乎所有事物 。 " 我們可以從那小到看不見的世界開始 " , 他說 。	we've stepped on the moon , we've mapped the continent , we've even gone to the bottom twice . what's left worth exploring ? biologists and nathan wolf asking the answer: almost everything . " we can start from that little to the world , " he said .
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	it's disease , it's state , it's microbial , it's geographical .

最近我去了威斯康星州的伯洛伊特市 。	i recently visited berloyte , wisconsin .
我去那裡是為了紀念一名20世紀的探險家 , 羅伊•查普曼•安德魯斯 。	i went there to commemorate a 20thcentury explorer , roy chapman andrews .
當他在美國自然歷史博物館的時候 , 安德魯斯領導了一系列對未知領域的探險 , 比如說在這裡的戈壁灘 。	when he was at the museum of natural history , andrews led a series of expeditions for the unknown , like the gobi beaches here .

我們現在知道病毒構成我們星球上絕大部分的遺傳資訊超過所有其他生命的遺傳資訊的總和 。	we now know that viruses make up most of the genetic information on our planet more than the sum of all other living genetic information .
而且顯然已經出現了無數有關病毒的切實應用在這個世界上--像天花的根除 , 子宮癌的疫苗的降臨--我們現在知道它大部分是由乳頭瘤病毒引起的 。	and it's clear that there's an enormous amount of incidence of virus applications in the world things like the eradication of smallpox , the vaccine decline in cervical cancer we now know that it's mostly caused by sarcoma .

也就是說當汽車都已經出現在世的時候 , 我們還不知道這種構成了我們星球上大部分的遺傳資訊的生物 。	that means that when the cars are already there , we don't yet know that this is the genetic information that makes up most of the genetic information on our planet .
我們現在有些很了不起的工具來幫助我們探索未知世界 , 像基因深度測序 , 可以讓我們不只是停留在表面來看自某個特定物種的獨立基因組 , 而是研究整個基因組--我們身體裡面和周邊無處不在的微生物群落 , 並且記錄下這些物種的遺傳資訊 。	we now have some amazing tools to help us explore the unknown world , like deep sequencing , that allow us not just to remain on the surface to look at the independent genomes of a particular species , but to study the entire genome the entire community of microbes that are everywhere in our bodies and document the genetic information of these species .
我們可以應用這些技術來研究從土壤到皮膚和它們中間的一切 。	we can use these techniques to study everything from soil to skin and everything in between .
在我所在的機構裡面 , 我們現在經常這麼做 , 來尋找暴發的原因 , 那些我們還不清楚的原因.	in my institutions , we do this now often to find the causes of this explosion , the reasons that we don't know .

如果我們開始仔細看看這些遺傳資訊 , 我們會看到一些常見的資訊當然了 , 有很多人類的遺傳資訊 , 但也有很多細菌和病毒的資訊 , 大部分是你鼻子裡面完全無害的東西 。	if we start looking at these genetic information , we see some common information , of course , a lot of human genetic information , but a lot of bacteria and viruses , mostly harmless things in your nose .
但我們也會看到一些非常非常讓人吃驚的東西 。	but we'll also see some very , very surprising things .

而且數量非常之多 。	and it's very large .

即使在相對無菌的血液裡 , 也有1%到2%的資訊是暗物質--無法被歸類 , 無法被判別類別 , 跟我們所見過的東西都不同 。	even in relatively sterile blood , one to two percent of the information is dark matter cannot be classified , cannot be categorized , cannot be categorized , is different from what we've seen .

我很高興的宣佈 , 和我的斯坦福、加州理工和舊金山加利福尼亞大學的同事們一起 , 我們正在開始開始一個新的行動去探索生物暗物質來尋找新生命的存在 。	i'm pleased to announce that with my colleagues at stanford and caltech and my colleagues at the university of san francisco california , we're starting a new action to explore the existence of biological dark matter .

daviddeutsch講述我們在宇宙中的位置	david deutsch tells us where we are in the universe .

因此我會努力達到這一點 。 但是我想先從大家都知道的兩件事說起 。	so i'm going to try to do that , but i want to start with two things that everybody knows .
第一件事 , 事實上這是從有記錄的歷史以來就眾所周知的事 。	the first thing , actually , is something that has been known for recorded history .
這就是地球 , 或者太陽系 , 或者說我們的環境 , 或諸如此類 , 獨一無二地適合維持我們的進化 , 或者說創造 , 正如我們之前所理解的一樣--適合我們當下的生存 , 最重要的是我們未來的生存 。	this is the earth , or the solar system , or our environment , or whatever , uniquely , suitable for our evolution , or creativity , as we've just understood earlier for the survival of our present , and most importantly for our future .

在這個概念裡 , 太空船之外宇宙不可調和地充滿敵意 , 而其內部是我們所賴以生存的一切 。	in this concept , the universe beyond the spaceship is filled with hostility , and inside is everything that we depend on .
我們只有一次機會:如果我們將我們的太空船折騰壞了 , 我們將無處可去 。	we only had one chance: if we tortured our spaceship , we would be everywhere .
第二件大家都知道的事是與我們在人類歷史中大部分時間所堅信的相反人類事實上並不是存在的中心 。	the second thing that everyone knows is that the opposite of what we believe in in human history is actually not the center of existence .
大家都知道stephenhawking說過我們只是存在於一個典型星球表面的一些化學汙垢這個典型星球環繞著一個典型恆星繞行太空 , 而這個典型恆星位於一個典型銀河系的邊緣 , 以此類推 。	you know , stephen hawking said that we are just a few chemical scums on the surface of a typical planet that orbits a typical star that orbits a typical star , and this typical star is on the edge of a typical galaxy , and so on .
大家都知道的兩件事當中的第一件大概是說我們存在於一個非常不典型的地方 , 獨一無二的適合性等 , 而第二件事卻說我們存在於一個典型的地方 。	the first of two things that everyone knows is probably that we live in a very untypical place , uniquely fit for equality , and the second thing that says we exist in a typical place .
尤其是當你將這兩件事當作生命中深刻的真理並以此作為你人生決策的依據 , 那麼他們似乎彼此有些衝突 。	and especially if you think of those two things as deep truths in your life and based on your life decisions , then they seem to have some conflict with each other .
但是這也沒法改變他們都是徹底錯誤的這一事實 。	but it doesn't change the fact that they're completely wrong .
他們就是錯誤的 。 讓我從第二件事說起:典型 。 讓我們看一下--這是一個典型的地方嗎 ? 讓我們看一下四周 , 如你所見 , 隨便超哪個方向望去 , 我們會看到一堵牆 , 還有一些化學汙垢----而這在宇宙中一點也不典型 。	they're just wrong . let me start with the second thing: typical . let's take a look at is this a typical place ? let's look around , as you can see , anywhere in the world , we'll see a wall , some chemical scum and it's not typical in the universe .
你所要做得是 , 朝著同一個方向前行數百英里然後往回看 , 你將根本不會看到任何牆或者化學汙垢--你所能看到是一個藍色星球 。 如果你繼續前行 , 你會看到太陽 , 太陽系 , 以及恆星等等 。	what you're doing is , you're walking hundreds of miles in the same direction , and you're going to look back , and you won't even see any walls or chemical scum you can see it's a blue planet . if you keep going , you'll see the sun , the solar system , and the stars and so on .
然而這在宇宙中仍然不算典型 , 因為恆星存在於星系中 。	but it's still not typical in the universe , because stars exist in galaxies .
宇宙中的大部分地方 , 或者說宇宙中一個典型的地方 , 不是任何靠近星系的地方 。	most places in the universe , or a typical place in the universe , are not anywhere near galaxies .
因此我們繼續前行 , 直到我們走出星系 , 然後再往回看 , 是的 , 你會看到巨大的星系 , 它螺旋形的觸手展現在我們面前 。	so we keep going , until we get out of the galaxy , and then we look back , yes , you'll see the giant galaxy , and it spirals in front of us right now .
而到達此地 , 我們已經跨越了十萬光年 。	and at this point , we've crossed 100 , 000 light years .
但是我們仍然一點也沒有靠近宇宙中的典型地方 。	but we're still not at all typical of the universe .
要到達典型地方 , 你需要跨越此距離的1000倍 , 直到你到達星系與星系中間的地方 。	to get to a typical place , you need to go 1 , 000 times that distance until you reach the middle of the galaxy and the middle of the galaxy .
那裡看上去是什麼樣子呢 ? 典型的 。	what does it look like ? typical .
那麼宇宙中一個典型的地方看上去是怎樣的呢 ?	so what does a typical place in the universe look like ?
在這裡 , ted不惜代價 , 給大家安排了一次高畫質晰的模擬的星系間空間的真實體驗--星系間空間的景觀 。	and here , at ted price , gives you a very highdimensional , simulated galaxy space the landscape of intergalactic space .
請將電燈關閉 , 我們就可以看到了 。	please turn the lights off , and we can see it .
不太準確 , 不是非常完美--看到了嗎 ? 星系間的空間--星系間的空間是徹底黑暗的 , 極端地黑暗 。 ♪	it's not quite accurate , not very perfect see , the intergalactic space between galaxies the space between galaxies is completely dark , extremely dark .
這個空間是如此的黑暗 , 假使你正盯著離你最近的恆星 , 這顆恆星正好發生超新星爆炸 , 當光線射到你的時候 , 假使你正直勾勾地盯著它看 , 你甚至連微弱的閃光都無法看到 。	this space is so dark , that if you're staring at the nearest star to you , this star is having a supernova explosion , and when the light hits you , if you're looking directly at it , you can't even see it even flashing .
宇宙就是如此的巨大和如此的黑暗 。	the universe is so massive and so dark .
這還沒有考慮超新星爆炸的光線是如此強烈和明亮 , 你在距離它數光年的地方會立馬斃命 。	it's not even considered the light that supernova explosions are so intense and bright , that you will be killed at a few lightyears away .
但是在星系間的空間 , 它是如此的遙遠 , 你甚至無法看見 。	but in intergalactic space , it's so far away , you can't even see it .
那裡也非常寒冷--不超過絕對零度三度 。	it's also very cold not more than three degrees above absolute zero .
什麼都沒有 。 那裡真空的濃度比目前地球上最好的技術可以產生的真空濃度的100萬分之一還要小 。 所以這就是宇宙裡一個典型的地方與這兒如何地不同 。	nothing . vacuum concentrations are smaller than one millionth the concentrations of vacuum that the best technology on earth can produce . so this is a typical place in the universe that's different from where it is .
也就是說我們現在所處的這個地方是如此地不典型 。	that's how untypical this place is right now .
請開燈 , 謝謝 。	please turn on the lights . thank you .
那麼我們如何瞭解距離我們如此遙遠的一個環境呢 ? 與我們所熟悉的一切相比 , 它是如此不同 , 如此陌生 。	so how do we make sense of an environment that's so far away , compared to everything we're used to , it's so different , so foreign .
地球--我們的環境 , 以我們這一形式存在--創造知識 。	the earth our environment , in our form , is creating knowledge .
這又意味著什麼呢 ? 向我們剛去過的地方的更遠處望去--我的意思是從這裡開始 , 利用望遠鏡--你會看到類似恆星的東西 。	what does that mean ? look at the further away from where we've been i mean from here , using telescopes you'll see things like stars .
他們叫做類星體 。 類星體原意是指類似恆星的物體 。	they're called quasars . galaxy bodies meant things like stars .
也就是說是指看上去有點像恆星的物體 。 但是他們不是恆星 。	in other words , it looks a little bit like stars , but they're not stars .
我們已經知道他們是什麼了 。 數十億年前 , 數十億光年之外 , 一個星系中心的物質朝著一個超級巨大的黑洞塌陷 。	we already know what they are . billions of years ago , a matter at the center of galaxy was collapsing at a supermassive black hole .
隨後密集的磁場對重力塌陷中的一些能量產生了導向作用 。 其中一些物質 , 以巨大的噴射流的形式逃離 , 照亮了宏偉的太空 , --我認為相當於一千億個太陽的光亮 。	and then intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy in some of the gravitational collapses , and some of the matter escaped in the form of giant jets and lit up the magnificent space i think that's the equivalent of 100 billion suns .
然而 , 與這樣一個噴射流的物理相比 , 我們人類大腦的物理大相徑庭到極點 。	however , compared to the physics of a jet like this , the physics of our human brain is extremely strong .
在這樣的環境裡 , 我們連一瞬間都無法生存 。 當我們試著描述那樣的噴射流中的狀況 , 語言變得無法表達 。	in such environments , we cannot survive instantaneously , when we try to describe the conditions in that jet , language becomes impossible to express .
這可能有點像經歷一次超新星爆炸 , 但是是在零距離接觸並且將數百萬年的能量集中到同一時間爆發 。	this may be a bit like experiencing a supernova explosion , but at zero distances and concentrating millions of years of energy at the same time .
但是 , 這個噴射流發生得如此地精確 , 以至於數十億年後在宇宙的另一端 , 一些化學汙垢可以準確地描述 , 建立模型 , 並預測和解釋 , 最重要的是--你可以找得到參考--現實中曾經發生過的事 。	but this jet takes place so precisely that billions of years later on the other side of the universe , some chemical scum can accurately describe and predict and explain , and most importantly you can find the reference what has happened in real life .
一個物理系統 , 大腦 , 包含了另外一個物理系統的準確工作模型--類星體 。	a physics system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of another physics system , quasars .
不僅僅是一個粗淺的影象 , 雖然也包含影象 , 而且還包含解釋性的模型 , 表達同樣的數學關係和一樣的因果結構 。	not only is it a shallow image , but it also contains an explanational model , expressing the same mathematical relationships as a causal structure .
這就是知識 。 如果這還不夠讓你驚訝的話 , 一個結構表達另外一個的準確性正隨著時間不斷提高 。 這就是知識的增長 。	this is knowledge . if this isn't surprising enough , one of the other accuracy is expressing accuracy over time . that's the growth of knowledge .
因此 , 物理規律擁有這樣一個特殊的性質 。	so physics has this unique property .
物體 , 不管他們彼此多麼相異 , 卻仍然能夠表現同樣的數學和因果結構 , 而且隨著時間增長表現得越來越多 。	objects , no matter how different they are , can still express the same mathematical and causal structure , and can perform more and more over time .
因此我們是與眾不同的化學汙垢 。 這一化學汙垢擁有普適性 。	so we're very different chemical scums . this one has universality .
它的結構準確度越來越高地包容著 , 世界萬物的結構 。 這個地方 , 不是宇宙中任何其他地方 , 在它自身內部 , 成為一個包容了其他一切宇宙萬物結構性和因果性精髓的中心 。 因此 , 意義深遠的是 , 物理規律允許這一現象 , 抑或甚至主導了它的發生這一事實是關於物理世界的最重要的事情之一 。	its structure is increasingly accuracy , the structure of everything , and this place , not anywhere else in the universe , is at the center of the structural and causal accuracy of all the other things that the universe has , and therefore , the physics allows this physics , or inhibits , or even dominates it , is one of the most important things about the physical world .
那麼太陽系--我們的環境 , 以我們的形式--是如何獲取這樣一個與宇宙其他部分的特殊關係的呢 ?	so how does the solar system our environment , in our form how does it acquire such a special relationship to the rest of the universe ?
stephenhawking觀點中其中一個正確面--我的意思是 , 這是正確的 , 但是著重點是錯的 。 其中一個正確面是它並沒有倚賴任何特殊的物理學 。 沒有特殊的放寬 , 沒有奇蹟發生 。 它的發生只依賴於我們現在富有的三種東西 。	stephen hawking's point of view is correct i mean , it's true , but it's wrong . one of the accurate aspects of it is that it doesn't depend on any special physics . there's no special amplification , there's no miracles . it just depends only on the three things that we've got now .
其中一個是物質 , 因為知識的增長是一種資訊處理的形式 。 資訊處理需要計算 , 計算需要電腦--現有的知識下不可能不需要物質來製造電腦 。	one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing ; information processing requires computation , computation requires computers impossible without matter to make computers .
我們還需要能量來製造電腦 , 最重要的是 , 要使得用來記錄我們所發現知識的媒介工作 。	we also need energy to make computers , and most importantly , to get the media to document the knowledge we've discovered .
第三種東西 , 較難感觸得到 , 但是在開放式的知識和解釋的開發中同樣關鍵的是證據 。	the third thing that's harder touch , but just as critical in openended knowledge and explanation development is evidence .
我們的環境中充滿了證據 。	our environment is filled with evidence .
但是我們常常忽略了測試--比如 , 牛頓的地球引力定律--大約是在300年前提出的 。	but we often miss trials things like newton's laws of gravity about 300 years ago .
但是我們習以為常的證據 , 從數十億年前就在地球上的每個角落裡不斷墜落 , 也會在接下來的數十億年裡繼續墜落 。 其他科學也同樣如此 。	but the evidence that we're used to , the evidence that's falling down everywhere on earth billions of years ago , will continue to fall over the next billion years , and so will other sciences .
就我們所知 , 發掘所有科學大部分基本真理的證據就在我們的星球上等待我們獲取 。	as far as we know , the evidence for the most fundamental truths of all science is just waiting on our planet to get us .
我們所在的地方充滿了證據 , 還有物質和能量 。	where we are is filled with evidence , and with matter and energy .
而在星系間的空間中 , 這三個創造開放式知識的前提條件存在的可能性極端之小 。	and in intergalactic spaces , these three precursors to create openended knowledge are the less likely to exist .
正如我所說 , 那裡空無一物 , 寒冷 , 黑暗 。 抑或不是如此 ?	as i said , where is the empty , the cold , dark , or not ?
事實上 , 這只是另外一個狹隘的誤解 。	in fact , this is just another narrow misunderstanding .
假想在星系間空間有一個立方體存在 , 與我們的房屋般大小 , 太陽系 。 以我們的標準來看 , 這個立方體非常空 , 但是它事實上仍然包含著超過百萬噸的物質 。	imagine there's a cube in intergalactic space , the size of our house , the solar system , and in our standards , it's very empty , but it actually contains more than a million tons of material .
一百萬噸足夠建造一個 , 比方說 , 自給自足的空間站 , 在這個空間站內聚居著一群科學家 , 他們致力於不斷創造開放式的知識 , 等等 。	a million tons is enough to build , say , a selfsustaining space station , a bunch of scientists who are working to create openended knowledge and so on .
然而 , 現在的科技甚至連從星系間空間收集氫氣和將其轉化成別的元素等都遠不能做到 。	however , even today's technologies gather hydrogen from intergalactic space and convert it to other elements and so on .
但問題是 , 在一個可理解的宇宙中 , 如果某事是物理定律所允許的 , 那麼在我們知道如何運作的情況下 , 什麼會妨礙我們去實踐它呢 ?	but the question is , in an understandable universe , if something is permitted by the laws of physics , then what would prevent us from doing it if we knew how ?
換句話說 , 這是一個關於知識的問題 , 而不是關於資源 。	in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .
同樣 , 如果我們可以做到的話 , 那麼我們將自動獲得能源供給 , 因為這裡的變化將是核反應堆--證據 ?	and if we can do that , then we automatically get the energy supply , because the change here is going to be the nuclear reaction evidence ?
還是一樣 , 對人類的感官來說那裡漆黑一片 。 但是你所需要做的是拿起一個望遠鏡 , 甚至是今天的技術設計 , 往外看去 , 你會看到我們從這兒看到的同樣的星系 。	or , again , it's dark for human senses , but what you need to do is pick up a telescope , even today's technology , and look out , and you'll see the same galaxies that we see from here .
如果你有一個更強大的望遠鏡 , 你將能看到恆星和行星 。	if you have a more powerful telescope , you'll see stars and planets .
在那些星系裡 , 你可以進行天體物理學研究 , 瞭解物理定律 。	in those galaxies , you can do astrophysics and learn the laws of physics .
在你所處的位置 , 你可以製造粒子加速器 , 研究初級粒子物理學 , 化學等 。	in your position , you can make particle accelerators , you can study primary particle physics , chemistry , etc .
也許最難做的科學研究是生物學實地考察 , 因為需要花費數百萬年才能往返最近的有生命的星球 。	perhaps the hardest science to do is biology field expedition , because it takes millions of years to get back to the nearest living planet .
但是我必須告訴你--對不起 , richard--但是我從來都不是那麼喜歡生物學實地考察 , 我想我們可以每數百萬年才進行一次 。	but i have to tell you sorry , richard but i never really liked biology field expeditions so much , i think we can do it every million years .
因此事實上 , 星系間空間並不具備創造開放式知識的前提條件 。 任何一個這樣的立方體 , 在宇宙中任何地方 , 都可以成為跟我們一樣的中心 , 如果履行這一計劃的知識確實存在的話 。	so in fact , intergalactic space doesn't have the premise to create an openended knowledge , and any cube like this , anywhere in the universe , can be the center like anywhere else in the universe , if the knowledge of this project exists .
因此我們並不是唯一熱情好客的地方 。	so we're not the only places to be passionate .
如果星系間空間可以創造出一串開放式的解說 , 那麼幾乎其它所有的環境都是可以的 。 地球也一樣 。 被汙染的地球也是一樣 。	if intergalactic spaces can create an openended list , then almost every other environment is ok , the earth is the same as the earth .
而限制性因素 , 這裡和那裡 , 不是資源 , 因為資源很充沛 , 而是知識 , 非常匱乏 。	and the limiting factors here and there , not resources , because resources are plentiful , but knowledge , very scarce .
這樣一個知識型的宇宙觀也許--我認為應該--讓我們感覺非常不平凡 。 但同時也讓我們感覺到自己的脆弱 , 因為這也意味著如果沒有那些必需的具體的知識來幫助我們應對宇宙中源源不斷地挑戰 , 我們將無法生存 。	such a cosmic view of knowledge may i think it should make us feel extraordinary , but it also makes us feel our vulnerability , because it also means that without the specific knowledge that we need to deal with the challenges of the universe , we will not survive .
僅僅是幾光年外的一個超新星爆炸 , 我們都將必死無疑 。	just a supernova explosion just a few lightyears away , we'll all be dead .
martinrees最近剛寫了一本關於我們人類對於所有事物的脆弱性的書 , 從天體物理學 , 到科學實驗事故 , 還有最重要的擁有大規模殺傷性武器的恐怖主義 。	martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all things , from astrophysics to scientific experiments , and most importantly , terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .
他認為人類文明只有50%的機率可以存活過這個世紀 。	he thinks that human civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .
我想他晚些時候會在這個會上給大家講述 。	i think he'll tell you a little bit later in this conference .
但是我認為這一問題並不適合用機率來描述 。	but i don't think the probabilities of this problem are adequate .
但是我同意他就此的看法 。 我們可以生存下去 , 我們也可能不會存續 。	but i agree with him that we can survive , and we may not survive .
但是這並不取決於機率 , 而是我們是否可以及時創造出相關的知識 。	but it doesn't depend on probability , it's whether we can create relevant knowledge in time .
這種危險肯定不是前所未有的 。 物種一直都在滅絕 。	this danger is certainly not unprecedented . species are extinction .
文明也會終止 。 絕大多數存在過的物種和文明都以成歷史 。	civilizations will end . the vast majority of existential species and civilizations are history .
如果我們想成為例外的話 , 邏輯上來看我們唯一的希望是利用將我們這個種群和文明與其他物種區別開的這個特徵 , 與其他一切都區別開的這個特徵 。 也就是 , 我們與物理定律得特殊關係 。 我們創造新的解釋和知識的能力--成為存在的中心 。	if we want to be an exception , logically , our only hope is to use the feature that distinguishes our group from civilization from other species , separates this from everything else , that is , we have a special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations and knowledge becomes the center of existence .
讓我將此運用到當前的一個論戰中 , 不是因為我想提議任何特定的解決方法 , 而只是用來闡明我所要講述的一些事 。	let me apply this to a current battle , not because i want to propose any particular solution , but just to illustrate some of the things that i'm going to talk about .
這個論戰就是全球暖化 。	this conference is global warming .
我是一個物理學家 , 但我並不是此領域的物理學家 。 就全球暖化來說 , 我只是個門外漢 。 對一個門外漢來說理智的做法是嚴肅對待權威的科學理論 。 而根據這一理論 , 已經太晚了 , 災難在所難免 。	i'm a physicist , but i'm not a physicist in this field , and as global warming , i'm just an outsider , and for an outsider , reasonable practice is a serious scientific theory to take authority , and it's already too late to be disastrous .
因為 , 如果我們目前最好的選擇是阻止二氧化碳排放的話 , 例如透過東京議定書之類的 , 限制經濟活動 , 以及花費千億美元等巨大的代價 , 那麼不管如何衡量 , 這就已經是一個災難了 。	because , if our best options at the moment are to stop co2 emissions from things like tokyo protocols and limiting economic activity and spending tens of billions of dollars on the economy , then it's already a disaster , no matter what measurements it .
倡議的行動甚至都不是為解決問題 , 而只是稍微推遲災難的到來 。 因此災難在所難免 , 一切都已晚 , 或在所有人意識到這個危險之前就已經太晚了 。	the actions that are advocated are not even solving problems , they're just a little bit of a disaster arrival , so disasters are already late , or they're too late to be aware of that danger .
上世紀70年代的時候也許就已經太晚了 , 那時候最先進的科學理論告訴我們工業排放將促成一個新的冰河世紀 , 數十億的人類將從此滅亡 。	it was too late in the 1970s , when the most advanced scientific theory industrial emissions were telling us that industrial emissions were going to lead to a new ice age , billions of humans were going to die .
這一教訓對我來說清晰可見 , 我不明白為什麼它沒有傳達至公眾辯論 。	this lesson was clear to me , and i didn't understand why it didn't reach public debate .
事實是我們不可能永遠知道 。 當我們知道有一個災難將要降臨 , 應對這個災難的成本要比災難本身小 , 那麼就真的沒有什麼好爭論的 。	the fact is that we can never know . when we know that a disaster is going to fall , there's going to be a disaster that's smaller than the cost of catastrophe , there's really nothing to argue about .
但是沒有任何預防措施 , 或者預防原則可以幫助我們避免我們還沒有預測到的問題 。	but no precaution or precautionary principle can help us avoid problems that we haven't predicted yet .
因此我們需要準備好去解決問題 , 而不僅僅是避免問題 。	so we need to be prepared to solve problems , not just to avoid problems .
一盎司的預防等於一盎司的解決 , 這是事實 , 但是這只是在我們知道預防什麼的情況下 。	an ounce of prevention equals an ounce of resolution , and that's true , but it's only in case we know what prevention is .
如果你的鼻子被打了一拳 , 醫學不會教你如何閃躲拳頭 。	if your nose is punched , medicine will not teach you how to hide your fists .
如果醫學不再研究治病的方法 , 而是僅僅研究預防 , 那麼它將幾乎一事無成 。	if medicine stops studying the cure , it's merely studying prevention , then it's almost impossible .
目前整個世界都在不計成本地忙著計劃來促成氣體排放量的減少 。	the whole world is now working to promote a decrease in gas emissions at all costs .
而它應該趕緊計劃如何降低溫度 , 以及計劃如何在溫度升高之後如何生存 。 不是不計成本 , 而是有效地、廉價的計劃 。 而這樣的一些計劃已經存在了 , 比如在太空中放置大批鏡子來將太陽光反射出去 , 以及刺激海洋生物消費更多的二氧化碳 。	and it's supposed to survive temperaturegrade , and how it's going to survive after temperature increases , not costeffectively , inexpensively and inexpensively , and some of these programs have already existed , such as putting big mirrors in space to reflect the sunlight away and to stimulate more carbon dioxide .
而目前 , 這些都只是邊緣研究 。	and so far these are just marginal studies .
人類在應對這個問題或者廣義上來說這些問題的時候 , 它們起不到核心作用 。	when humans respond to these questions or in general , they don't have the core effects .
對於我們並未知覺的問題 , 糾錯的能力--不是無限期的躲過期發生的絕對好運--是我們唯一的希望 , 不僅僅是為解決問題 , 而是為生存 。	the ability to tackle problems that we don't realize aren't indefinitely good luck is our only hope , not just for problemsolving but for survival .
我們應該拿起兩塊石碑 , 在上邊刻上銘文 。	we should pick up two stones , put inscriptions up there .
其中一塊刻上 " 問題是可以解決的 " 。	one of them is: " problems are solvable . "
另外一塊刻上 " 問題是不可避免的 " 。	the other piece is: " the problem is inevitable . "
被困在不健全的制度下 , 一個國家怎麼可能脫貧呢 ? 經濟學家paulromer提出全新見解: " 特別市 " , 由多國聯合政府管理的、城市規模的管理區域 。	how could a country be stuck with institutions that were impoverished , and the economist paul romer raised a new insight: special markets , governed by multinational united nations , urban administration ?
business , culture , economics , globalissues , politics	those are the people of the world , the issues , the people of the world .
paulromer的全新見解:特別市	paul romer's new insight: special markets .
請看這張圖片 。	i'll show you this picture .
它帶給我們一個極具吸引力的謎 。	it gives us a very attractive mystery .
這些非洲學生在做功課在首都機場的街燈下因為他們家裡沒有電 。	these african students are doing homework under the streetlights of the capital airport because they don't have electricity at home .

拿那個穿綠襯衫的學生做例子 ,	take that student in green shirt .
假設他的名字叫做nelson 。	let's say his name is nelson .
我猜他肯定有個手機	i guess he's got a phone .
有趣的是 ,	and here's what's interesting .
為什麼nelson有機會享用像手機這樣的前沿科技成果但卻不能在家用上電力 ? 人們早在100年前就已經發明瞭這一科技啊 ?	why did nelson have the opportunity to use coastal technology like mobile phones , but not on home electricity , where people had invented this technology 100 years ago ?
答案是 " 制度 " 。	the answer is rules .
不健全的制度會妨礙這種雙贏節決辦法的產生人們在一定的制度之下就不會將科技帶給像nelson這樣的人	unhygiency prevents this winwin resolution from generating people in a certain institution that doesn't bring technology to people like nelson .
什麼樣的制度呢 ?	what systems ?
這個國家的電力公司需要遵守一條制度這個制度要求它在政府補貼的條件下從使用者收取極其低價電費事實上 , 電費便宜到另電力公司虧損的地步	the power company in this country needs to follow an institution that requires it to charge extremely low electricity prices from the user's subsidies , and in fact , electricity is cheap to the loss of alternatives .
所以 , 電力公司既沒有資源 , 也沒有動機去給使用者接通電源	so , the power company has no resources , no motivation , to connect the user .
總統想要改變這個局面	the president wanted to change this .
他已經覺察到更換體制是具可能性的 。 能讓商家盈利的體制才能使有動機爭取更多使用者	he has noticed that the change institutions is possible , that the systems that make merchant profit in order to motivate more users .
賣nelson的手機的那個廠家也正式在制度下經營著	the facility that sells nelson's cell phone is also running institutions .
總統已經領會到制度執行良好	the president has led the systems well .
所以他嘗試著改變現行的電價制度但來自商人以及消費者的反對的聲音四起他們想保留現行的補貼電費制度	so he's trying to change the price of current electricity , but it comes from businesspeople and consumer opposing sounds all the way around , and they want to retain the current patch system .
總統無能為力 , 只能任由現行制度阻止雙贏局面產生 , 任由它妨礙改善國家	the president couldn't do anything about it , and it was created by the current system to stop the winwin situation from improving the country .

我想說 , 我們可以把抽象化為實際或者說 , 如果我們給予人民更多選擇給予領導者更多選擇 , 領導者在很多國家也是人民麼	i want to say that we can make abstraction possible , or if we give people more choices to leaders , to give leaders more choice , leaders are also people in many countries .

中國最明亮的地域你可以在輪廓的邊際看到是香港	the brightest area in china , you can see it on the outline , hong kong .
香港其實是中國很小的一塊地方在二十世紀的絕大部分時期都在非常不同的體制下治理著與大陸其它地方都不同體制是從當時有效的市場經濟複製出來的並由英國治理	hong kong is actually a very small piece of china that governed institutions very , very different institutions over the vast majority of the 20th century , and different institutions from the rest of the continent were copied from the market economy at the time ,
於19世紀五十年代 , 香港是百萬大陸人去找像縫紉 , 製作玩具之類工作的地方	in the 1950s , hong kong was a millionaire continent looking for places like sewing , making toys , doing things like that .
但要想提高收入提高技術促進飛速增長	but to increase income , we need to increase the speed of growth .
香港也是像鄧小平這樣的領導者想要使大陸走向市場經濟時要模仿的經濟模型	hong kong is also leaders like deng xiaoping want to mimic the economic model of how to move the continent to the market economy .

但像城市就能給你這些機會來建立新領域開拓新體制 , 人們可以選擇	but cities can give you opportunities for building new areas , for new institutions , for people to choose .

首先綱領詳細說明所有的條例規則來吸引那些建設特別市的人才	first of all , syllabus details all the rules to attract people who build special markets .

要做到給領導者自由我們需要允許國家間的合作讓不同的國家可以合作事實上像中國和英國合作一樣來首先建設一個市場經濟的飛地然後擴大至整個中國	to achieve freedom for leaders , we need to allow different countries to work together , to actually build a market economy for the first time , to grow to china .
或多或少 , 英國 , 不經意地在上個世紀它治理香港期間對削減世界貧困上做出了比任何支援專案都更為卓越的貢獻	more or less , britain , inadvertently , in the last century , has done a more extraordinary contribution to the world's poverty reduction in hong kong than any support project .
所以只要我們允許這樣的合作重演我們可以將這個效應擴大的整個世界的規模	so if we allow this kind of collaboration to reproduce , we can scale this across the world .
有時這需要委派職責一種從一個國家到另外一個國家的責任的委派來執行某些行政管理的職責	sometimes it takes a duty of commitment , a duty of responsibility from one country to another , to run some administrative accounts .
我這麼說你們中有些人可能開始想 " 那 , 不是要恢復殖民主義嗎 ? "	and i say that some of you are probably starting to think , " well , wouldn't it restore colonialism ? "
不是的 。 但是認識到這種情緒卻是重要的我們開始考慮這些時 , 這些情緒將產生會阻礙我們扼殺我們的能力我們探索新想法的興趣	it's not . but it's important to recognize that emotions are going to stifle our capacity to explore new ideas .
為什麼這不是殖民主義 ?	why is this not colonialism ?

這與稀有物質不同分享意味著每人得到少一些	it's very different from rare material sharing , which means less for each person .

從艱苦漫長的環球探險中 , 基因組學先驅克雷格•文特忙裡偷閒 , 為我們講述其團隊描繪海洋生物多樣性的歷程 。 到目前為止 , 他們已經發現了數百萬的基因 。	from a long , long global adventure , genomics pioneered craig venter busy talking about the journey of marine biodiversity for us , and so far , they have found millions of genes .
dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , invention , oceans , science , technology	dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , welcome , marine .
克雷格•文特:dna和海洋	craig venter: dna and the ocean .
休息的時候 , 有幾個人過來問我對老齡化問題怎麼看	at the break , a couple of people came to ask me what i think about aging .
我的唯一看法是	my only opinion was this .
我認為樂觀主義者比悲觀主義者活得久得多	i think optimists live much longer than pessimists .
在這18分鐘裡我將告訴你們的是我們是如何做到從最初的閱讀遺傳編碼發展到我們自己開始編寫遺傳編碼	in those 18 minutes , what i'm going to show you is how we've gone from reading genetic code to encoding ourselves .
僅僅十年之前的這個月我們發表了第一個來自自由活動生命體的基因序列即流感嗜血桿菌的序列	this month only a decade ago , we published the first freely active genome sequence of life , the sequence of haemophilus .
由此我們將基因組專案完成的時間從13年降到4個月	so we've gone from 13 years down to four months .
現在 , 同樣的基因組專案只需要2到8個小時	now , the same genome project only takes two to eight hours .
因此過去十年 , 我們完成了大量的基因組測序大部分的人類病原體幾種植物多種昆蟲和哺乳動物包括人類基因組	so over the last decade , we've done a lot of sequencing genomes , most of human pathogens , several plants , multiple insects and mammals ,
約在十年前我們對基因組學發展的設想是到今年年底的時候我們或許能完成3到5個基因組的測序而事實上已經完成了數百個	and about a decade ago , our assumptions about genomics were that by the end of this year , we might be able to sequence three to five genomes , and in fact , hundreds of them have been completed .
我們剛剛從戈登-貝蒂•摩爾基金會獲得一筆資助作為環境有機體專案的副專案我們將在今年完成130個基因組的測序	we just got a grant from the gordon betty moore foundation as a subject project for environmental organisms projects , and we're going to sequence 130 genomes this year .
閱讀遺傳編碼的速率已然改變	the rate of reading genetic code has changed .
但我們看到 , 未來的路還很長我們僅僅探索了這個星球表面上淺淺的一層	but what we see is that the future is very long , and we're only exploring the shallow layers of the shallow surface of the planet .
大多數人沒有意識到這些肉眼看不到的生物微生物構成了地球約一半的生物量而所有的動物加起來也才佔地球生物量的千分之一	most people don't realize that the microbes that you can't see make up about half the biomass of the earth , and all animals add up to a thousandth of the biomass of the earth .
跑到海邊喝上一口海水或許不是牛津人經常做的事但請記住每一毫升的海水裡有大約一百萬個的細菌其中的病毒更是以千萬計	running to the beach , drinking seawater may not be something that oxfords do a lot , but remember that every single milliter of seawater , there's about a million bacteria , and the viruses are thousands of them .
兩年前只有不到五千種的微生物被鑑定歸類於是我們決定做些這方面的事情	less than 5 , 000 microbes were identified two years ago , so we decided to do something about it .
我們啟動了巫師二號考察和其他大型的海洋考察活動一樣我們嘗試每200英里採一次樣	we launched a wizard ii expedition , like any other big ocean expedition , and we tried to sample every 200 miles .
考察伊始 , 我們在百慕大進行了測試專案然後前往哈利法克斯接著到美國東海岸加勒比海、巴拿馬運河穿過加拉帕哥斯群島 , 然後橫跨太平洋現在我們正在穿越印度洋的過程中	we tested it in bermuda , and then headed to hallefax , and then the east coastal caribbean , the panama canal , running through the galapagos , and across the pacific , now we're in the process of going across the indian ocean .
工作很艱難 , 我們乘著一艘帆船某種程度上我們想透過它激起年輕人投身科學的興趣	it's hard work . we're sailing boats in a sailing vessel , and in a way we want to be interested in getting young people into science .
實驗其實非常簡單	the experiments are actually very simple .
採集海水 , 過濾用不同的過濾器採集不同大小的生物然後把它們的dna帶回羅克韋爾的實驗室在那裡我們可以每24小時測完一億字元的遺傳編碼	take seawater , filter different filters , take different size organisms , and then take their dna back to rockwell's lab , where we can measure the genetic code every 24 hours .
透過這些我們已經有了一些驚人的發現	and we've made some surprising discoveries through this .
比如我們眼睛裡的視色素之前認為自然界中只有一到兩種生物擁有和我們一樣的視色素	for instance , pigments in our eyes used to think that only one or two organisms in nature have the same pigments that we have .
但後來發現在溫暖海區的上層海水中幾乎每個物種都擁有這類光受體並利用陽光作為能量來源和交流工具	but it turns out that in the upper waters of the warm seas , almost every species has these light receptors and use sunlight as a source and a communication tool .
僅僅一個採集點 , 從一桶水中我們就能發現1300萬個新基因相當於5萬個新種	just one collection , and from a barrel of water , we can see that 13 million new genes are equivalent to 50 , 000 new ones .
藉助來自斯隆基金會的資助我們已經將研究擴充套件到空氣中	by funding from the sloan foundation , we've expanded research into the air .
我們正在測算 , 在我們每天呼吸的空氣中漂浮著多少病毒和細菌特別是在飛機和禮堂等封閉環境中	we're calculating how many viruses and bacteria float in the air we breathe every day , especially in closed environments like airplanes and auditoriums .
我們透過一些簡單的儀器進行過濾在紐約市某棟建築的頂上僅用一天我們就過濾出數十億計的微生物	we filtered billions of microbes on top of a building in new york city just a day .
目前我們正在對它們進行測序	we're currently sequencing them .
單純從資料蒐集方面僅僅在加拉帕戈斯群島我們就發現幾乎每200英里我們都能從採集的樣品中看到巨大的多樣性	just from the data collection , just from the galapagos islands , we've discovered that almost every 200 miles , we can see enormous diversity in the samples that are being collected .
不同的溫度梯度或許可以部分解釋這種多樣性	different temperature gradients may well be explaining a little bit about this diversity .
這是一張基於溫度的衛星圖片紅色表示溫暖區域藍色表示冷的區域我們發現 , 在溫暖海水中獲得樣品與冷海水中的樣品在物種的豐富程度上具有極大的差異	this is a temperature satellite based on the temperature image , showing warm areas in red , cool areas in blue , and what we found was that the samples and samples in the warm water were very different in the abundance of the species .
另一個讓我們感到驚奇的事情是這些光受體能探測到不同波長的光而我們能透過它們的氨基酸序列來推測這一過程	another surprising thing to us is that these light receptors can detect light from different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that through their amino acid sequences .
不同區域之間 , 它們也差別巨大	and they're enormously different .
或許不是很讓人驚奇在幾乎是幽藍的深海里光受體傾向於 " 看 " 到藍光	it may not be surprising that in nearly humorous deep seas , receptors tend to look at blue light .
而當週圍存在大量葉綠素的時候它們則 " 看 " 到許多綠光	and when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .
在向較極端的紅外和紫外波段移動時光受體的差別可能更大	when the light moves towards the extreme infrared and the ultraviolet period , the receptors may be even larger .
為了對我們採集的所有基因進行評估我們彙總了所有資料包括到目前為止考察所得的所有資料代表了地球上超過一半的基因資料總共約2900萬個基因	to evaluate all of the genes that we've collected , we've collected all of the data , including all of the data from our expeditions so far represents 29 million genetic data on the planet .
我們把這些基因放入基因家族中試圖回答:我們是發現了已知基因家族中的新成員還是發現了新的基因家族 ?	we put those genes into the family , and we try to answer: did we discover new members of the known genome , or did we discover new gene family members ?
結果表明我們找到了大約5萬個主要的基因家族但我們從環境中獲得的每個新樣品都只是對這些新基因家族的線性補充	it turns out we found about 50 , 000 primary gene families , but every new sample that we obtained from the environment was just linearly addressing these new gene families .
因此我們正處在發現地球生命及其組成部分和基因基礎的最初階段	so we're in the earliest stages of discovering the earth's life and its components and its genetic base .
我們來看下所謂的進化樹我們人類就在右上角 , 和動物們在一起	we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , and we humans are in the upper righthand corner , with animals .
在動物界約2900萬個基因中我們的基因組才僅僅擁有24000個基因	in the animal kingdom , we only have 2 , 4 , 000 genes in the animal kingdom .
如果把所有的動物算在一起我們與之分享著不到30000可能在1.2萬或再多數千的不同的基因家族	if we calculate all the animals together , we share less than 3 , 000 animals with them , possibly 12 , 000 , or tens of thousands of different gene families .
現在我不僅僅將這些基因視為進化的設計元件	now , i don't just think of these genes as design components of evolution .
而且我們要從 " 基因中心觀點 " 或許要追溯到理查德•道金斯的理論而非 " 基因組中心觀點 " 來思考它們對這些基因元件的構造方式是不同的	and we're going to go back to richard dawkins' theory of the genomecentric perspective , rather than the genomecentric perspective , to think about how these genetic components are made of different things .
合成dna , 即人工合成dna的能力在過去的十年或二十年裡與dna測序的能力在某種程度上是同步發展的而且都變得越來越快速和廉價	synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , in the last decade or two , has been synchronizing with dna sequencing in a way that's getting faster and cheaper .
有關合成基因組的想法是在1995年我們對第二個基因組即生殖道支原體測序的時候想到的	the idea for the synthetic genome was in 1995 , and it came to us when we sequenced the second genital genital colony , the genital colony .
我們還製作了相當不錯的t恤寫著 , " 我愛惜我的生殖器 "	we also made a pretty good tshirt that said , " i love my genitalia . "
這其實只不過是個微小的生物	it's just a tiny creature .
卻擁有近500個基因	it has nearly 500 genes .
嗜血桿菌擁有1800個基因	haemophilus has 1 , 800 genes .
我們提出疑問如果某物種需要800個基因 , 另一種需要500個是否能用一套更小的基因組成一個微小的可運作生命系統	we asked if one species needed 800 genes , the other 500 , to be able to use a smaller set of genomes to make a tiny , tiny , operating system .
於是我們開始做轉座子的突變發生	so we started mutationizing our seats .
轉座子是隨機插入遺傳編碼之中的短的dna片段	the rotating seat is short pieces of dna that randomly inserts into the genetic code .
如果轉座子插入到基因中間 , 就會擾亂基因的功能	if you insert a seat in the middle , it disrupts the function of the gene .
因此我們找出所有能夠接受轉座子插入的基因併為這些 " 非必需基因 " 製作了 " 地圖 "	so we looked at all the genes that could be inserted into these , and they wouldn't have to be necessarily made a map .
但結果我們發現環境對此的影響非常關鍵我們只能根據環境中確實存在的條件來定義必需和非必需基因	but it turns out that the environment is very critical to this , and we can only define the unnecessary and nonnecesary genes according to the conditions that exist in the environment .
我們還試圖做一個更直觀的研究對13個有親緣關係的生物我們試圖比較它們的基因組 , 看它們是否有相同之處	we also tried to do a more straightforward study of 13 organisms with relationships , and we tried to compare their genomes to see if they had the same thing .
於是我們得到了這些重疊的圓圈 , 我們發現只有173個基因在這所有13種生物中是相同的	so we got these overlapping circles , and we found out that only 173 genes are the same in all 13 species .
如果忽略掉一個細胞內寄生物的話這個基因庫還能擴充套件一點當我們審視核心的一組約310個基因時基因庫擴大更多	if you ignore a parasite in a cell , this gene bank can expand a little bit , and when we look at the core set , it's about 310 genes , and the gene pool expands even more .
因此我們認為可以從最少500個基因擴充套件或縮小取決你怎麼看這個問題到約300到400個基因	so we think we can go from the least 500 gene expansion kits or minimum gene expansion or minimum determination of what you're looking at , to something like 300 or 400
證明這些理論的唯一方法是以這些基因人工構建一個染色體而且我們必須用基於表達框的方式來達到這一目的	the only way to prove these theories is to build a chromosome in these genes , and we have to do it based on the framework .
我們發現大片段精確合成dna是非常非常困難的	it turns out that big pieces of synthetic dna are very , very difficult .
我的同事漢姆•史密斯和克萊德•哈欽森發明了一個讓人振奮的新方法能讓我們在短短兩週時間內合成一個擁有5000個鹼基對的病毒而且在基因序列和生物學特性上都百分百精確	my colleague , han smith and clay harchinson , have invented an exciting new way that we can synthesize a virus that has 5 , 000 base pairs in just two weeks , and 100 percent precisely in gene sequencing and biology .
那是個相當讓人興奮的實驗:我們僅僅把合成的dna片段注進細菌中 , 突然之間dna就開始引導病毒顆粒的合成而病毒反過來殺死了細菌	it was a pretty exciting experiment: we just injected synthetic dna fragments into bacteria , and all of a sudden , dna started guiding viral particle synthesis , and viruses came back and killed bacteria .
這並非第一個合成的病毒一年前已有某種脊髓灰質炎病毒被製造了出來但這卻是唯一達到百分之一活性的病毒耗時三年才合成成功	it's not the first synthetic virus that was made a year ago , but it's the only one percent active virus that took three years to synthesize .
這是phix-174結構的一個動畫	this is a animation of the structure of phi x174 .
這是軟體為自己構建硬體的活例子也為我們的生物學提供了新想法	this is a living example of software that constructs our hardware and provides new ideas for our biology .
有人立即開始擔心生物武器的威脅不久前我也在參議院委員會和另一個由美國政府成立旨在評價這一領域的特殊委員會上作證	immediately , i was worried about the threat of biological weapons , and not long ago , i was at the senate committee and another special committee that the u . s . government was authorized on .
我認為最重要的是將事實牢記在心而非人們對事情發生的想象	i think the most important thing is to keep facts in mind , not what's happening .
基本上 , 任何現在已經被測序的病毒其基因組都可以被合成	essentially , any virus that has been sequenced now can be synthesized .
人們立馬被埃博拉病毒或天花病毒之類等嚇壞了但從這些生物體中提取的dna並不具有感染力	people were terrified by things like the ebola virus or smallpox , but the dna extracted from these organisms was not contagious .
因此即使有人制成了天花病毒基因組其dna本身並不會引發感染	so even if someone made the smallpox genome , its dna doesn't cause the infection itself .
安全部門真正需要擔心的是 " 設計者病毒 "	the security department really needs to worry , " designer virus . "
只有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯曾經花大力氣致力於生物武器的研製	only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , have spent an effort working on biological weapons .
如果這些研究真的已經終止那麼在未來人為製造出設計者病毒的機率微乎其微	if these studies have actually stopped , the odds of making designer viruses in the future are slightly less likely .
我想兩年內製造出單細胞生物是可能的	i think in two years , it's possible to make singlecelled organisms .
而真核細胞我們自己擁有的這種細胞也可能在十年內製造出來	and the real nuclear cells that we have can be made in a decade .
我們可以區分開進入這個人工基因組的不同表達框和不同基因使得我們能構建數十種不同的結構	we can separate into the boxes and different genes of this artificial genome , allowing us to build dozens of different structures .
關鍵是 , 如何把所有其他的放進來 ?	the key thing is , how do you put in all the others ?
我們從這些片段開始然後透過一個同源重組系統將其組合到染色體中	we start with these clips , and then we combine them with a homologous recombination system into a chromosome .
這來自一種名為耐輻射奇異球菌的生物能在三百萬拉德的輻射劑量下保持活力	this comes from a creature called deinococcus radiodurans that remain vital for three million rads .
在暴露輻射約12到24小時其染色體幾乎完全破碎的情況下它還能將自身的染色體重新組裝起來	in exposure radiation for about 12 to 24 hours , its chromosome was almost completely broken , and it could reassemble its own chromosomes .
這種生物在地球上幾乎無處不在甚至由於人類的活動它們還可能在外太空活動	these organisms are almost everywhere on earth , and even because of human activity , they may be active in outer space .
這是玻璃燒杯在約50萬拉德輻射下的情形	this is a glass burning glass in about half a million rads .
玻璃開始燃燒 , 爆裂而位於底部的微生物則似乎越來越開心	glass starts to burn , burns , and microbes at the bottom seem to be getting happier and happier .
這是實際的情形上面是經過170萬拉德輻射之後的染色體	this is a practical scenario with a chromosome after 17 million rads of radical radiation .
幾乎已經支離破碎	it was almost broken .
下面是24小時之後同樣的dna自動重組的結果	and here's the same dna automatically recombined 24 hours later .
這些生物能做到的真是歎為觀止 。 如果不是數以萬計的話也許我們還能找到數以千計的物種也同樣能夠做到	these organisms are truly marvelous . if not tens of thousands , maybe we'll be able to find thousands and thousands of other species to do the same .
這些基因組合成之後第一步就是將它們移植到另一個沒有基因組的細胞中	the first step after these genomes are to transplant them into cells with no other genomes .
因此我們認為合成細胞將具有巨大的前景不僅僅在生物學基礎的理解上而且很可能幫我們應對環境和社會問題	so we think that synthetic cells are going to have huge promise not just in biologybased understanding , but possibly in environmental and social problems .
例如 , 從我們測序的第三種生物詹氏甲烷球菌 , 生活在相當於水沸點的高溫中以氫作為能量來源並依靠捕獲環境中的二氧化碳為自己提供所需的碳	for instance , from our third species , methane bacterio , living at the equivalent of high temperatures at the boiling point of water , using hydrogen as a source of energy , and depending on capturing carbon dioxide in the environment , carbon
由此可知 , 透過大量不同的途徑數以千計的生物能夠捕獲並依賴二氧化碳生存	and therefore , thousands of organisms can be captured and dependent on carbon dioxide .
因此我們可以透過捕獲大氣中的碳製造生物高聚物或其他產品來替代從石油中工業合成的碳製品	so we can replace carbon products that are synthesized from carbon in the atmosphere by capturing carbon in the atmosphere , or other products .
有種依賴一氧化碳的生物我們利用其還原能力使水分子破裂 , 製造出氫和氧	there's an organism that depends on carbon oxide , and we use its ability to crack the water molecule and make hydrogen and
同樣 , 還有許多途徑能夠用來轉化甲烷	similarly , there are many ways to convert methane .
杜邦公司和挪威石油公司有一大型專案就是把挪威油氣田中的甲烷轉化為有用的產品	the largest project for dupont and norwegian oil is to convert methane from the oil fields in norway into useful products .
我突然想到 , 將有一個新的領域 " 組合基因組學 " 很快就要誕生因為有了這些新的合成方法有了這麼龐大的基因序列和同源重組我們可以設計出一個能夠每天生產近百萬個染色體的機器人	and it struck me that there was a new field called combinatoric genomics that was going to be born very quickly , because with these new methods of synthesizing , we had these huge genome sequences and homologous recombinations , we could design a robot that could produce nearly a million chromosomes a day .
因此 , 所有的生物學特徵都能透過螢幕來選擇無論是製造氫化學合成 , 或者僅僅是生存能力	so all the biology features can be chosen through screens , either by making hydrogen synthesis , or just by making survival .
理解這些基因的功能將變得觸手可及	understanding the function of these genes will become a tentacle .
我們正嘗試改進光合作用以直接在陽光下製造出氫	we're trying to improve photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly in the sun .
光合作用受氧調節而我們使用的對氧不敏感的氫化酶將完全改變這一過程	photosynthesis is oxygenregulated , and the unsensitive hydrogen enzymes we use are going to completely change the process
我們還整合了多種纖維素酶這些酶可以把複雜的糖類分解為簡單的糖類並在同一個細胞內發酵產生酒精	we also integrated multiple cellulose enzymes , which enzymes can break down complex sugars into simple sugars , produce alcohol in the same cell .
在一些大型的實驗室裡已經開始利用微生物進行藥品生產	in some large laboratories , microbes are starting to use drug production .
環境中化合物的化學比我們最好的化學家制造出來的化合物還要複雜很多	the chemistry of the environment is much more complicated than our best chemists make up compounds .
也許未來的工程物種將成為我們的食物來源能量來源環境補救手段甚至取代石化行業	perhaps future engineering species will be our food source energy sources , environmental remedies , and even replace the fossil industry .
最後讓我以道德和政策上的研究結束吧	let me end with moral and policy studies .
我們推遲了1999年開始的實驗直到對是否應該嘗試製造人工物種這一問題進行了一年半的生物倫理學討論後實驗才繼續進行	we launched our experiments in 1999 , until the question of whether we should try to make artificial species , and it took about a year and a half of the bioethical discussions to go on .
每個主要宗教都參與其中	every major religion is involved .
真是一項奇怪的研究因為許多宗教領袖都以他們的教義、經文作為法律而且不能從中找出禁止製造生命的條文所以這應該沒什麼問題最根本的擔憂來自生物武器方面但只有開始進行這些實驗之後我們才能找出從事這一切的原因	it's a strange study , because many religious leaders are using their customs , their scriptures , and they can't find the protocols that prohibit life , so there's nothing wrong with this very fundamental worrying comes from biological weapons , but only when we do these experiments , we can figure out what's going on .
目前斯隆基金會已經資助了一個相關的多機構參與的研究以確定這些實驗給社會帶來的風險和益處同時也為像我們這樣的科學團隊在這一領域開展研究制定規則在前進的同時我們也努力成為一個良好的榜樣	now , the sloan foundation has funded a multiinstitutional study to identify the risks and benefits of these experiments and to build the research teams like ours , and to build the rules forward , and we're also trying to be a good example .
有許多複雜的議題	there's a lot of complex issues .
除了生物恐怖主義它們其實都很簡單:我們能否設計出生產清潔能源的工具透過各種不同的簡單步驟或能徹底改變發展中國家的能源生產模式	in addition to bioterrorism , they're actually very simple: can we design tools to produce clean energy through various simple steps , or can we radically change the energy production model in the developing world ?
心理學家philipzimbardo說我們大部分人都忽略了幸福和成功的來源:那就是我們觀望過去、面向現在和展望未來 。 要想改善生活質量 , 他建議我們首先要調整時間觀念 。	the psychologist philip zimbardo says that most of us are neglecting the source of happiness and success: that's what we're looking at the past , facing the present and the future , and to improve the quality of life , he suggests we have to adjust our time .

philipzimbardo健康的時間觀念	philip zimbardo's time perspective .
我想跟你們分享一些對時間的神秘力量的看法當然是在很短的時間內	i want to share with you some of the mysterious powers of time , of course , in a very short period of time .

philipzimbardo:讓我們來看看這段對話是有關 " 亞當的誘惑 "	philip zimbardo: let's take a look at this conversation about " adam's temptation . "
快 , 亞當 , 別磨磨<unk>的 , 就咬一口 , 我已咬過了	soon , adam , don't mill , just bite , i've bitten .
就一口 , 亞當 。 不要放棄夏娃	just one bite , adam . don't give up eve .
我不知道啊	i don't know .
我真的不想惹麻煩	i really didn't want to get in trouble .
好吧 , 就一口 。 能怎麼樣 ?	okay , just one bite . what can we do ?
生活中充滿了誘惑 。 而且到處都是:屈服或反抗是、不是、現在、隨後、衝動、沉穩專注現在和展望未來	life is filled with temptation , and everywhere: submission or resistance , is it , is it , present , impulsive , steady focus , now and our future .
激情時刻一旦到來 , 道德束縛將皆被打破	when the passions come , the moral constraints will be broken .
那些承諾婚前無性行為的女孩–這裡感謝下小布什總統大多數 , 大概百分之六十的人在一年之內就違背了自己的承諾	those girls who promised to have sex without marriage thanks to president george bush , most people , about 60 percent of them , had violated their commitments within a year .
而這些人幾乎沒采取任何 " 安全措施 "	and these people have barely accepted any safety measures .
多麼多的承諾啊	what a promise .
現在我們來試試引誘4歲的孩子 , 拿他們來做個試驗	now let's try this with a fouryearold . let's do an experiment with them .
他們現在有一個棉花糖 , 如果他們能夠等到實驗員回來再吃的話 , 就可以得到2個棉花糖	they now have a marshmallow , and if they can wait for the experimenter to come back , they'll get two marshmallows .
這當然是需要付出的 , 如果你真喜歡吃棉花糖的話 , 那就等著	of course it's necessary to pay if you really like to eat marshmallow .
但結果是3分之2的孩子屈服於誘惑	but it turns out that twothirds of the children submit to temptation .
他們等不了 。 當然 , 其它的孩子都得到了第二個棉花糖	they couldn't wait . and of course , all the other kids got the second marshmallow .
因為他們抵抗了誘惑 。 他們甘於先苦後甜 。	because they resisted temptation . they sweet .
沃特米塞奇 , 是我在斯坦福大學的同事他在14年後重新找到這些孩子並去勘察他們現時的情況	walter mitch , my colleague at stanford university who , 14 years later , reclaimed these children and explored what was happening to them .
結果發現這兩組孩子在各個方面都有著巨大的差異	and it turns out that these two groups have enormous differences in many ways .
那些等到了第二個棉花糖的孩子在sat中比另一組得分平均高250分	the children who waited for the second marshmallow were 250 points higher than the other group at the sat .
這是多麼大的差異啊 ! 這根本就是兩組智商水平不同的孩子啊	it's a huge difference . it's a different group of i . q . kids .
他們都沒有任何問題 , 都是好學生	they don't have any problems . they're good students .
他們自信而且果斷 。 那麼今天我所要說的關鍵是同樣也是你們的關鍵點就是由 " 面向現在 " 轉變為 " 展望未來 "	they're selfconfident and decisive . so the key thing i'm going to talk about today is that it's also your critical point , which is to turn from " the present " to " the future . "
那什麼是時間洞察力呢 ? 這將是我下面要講的	so what is time perspective ? that's what i'm going to talk about .
時間洞察力是研究個人包括我們在內 , 如何以時間區域或時間類別為單位劃分自身的經歷體驗 。	time perspective is the study of individuals , including us , how to divide our experiences in time zones or time categories .
其實我們一直都在自然而然地做著	we've been doing it naturally .
而影響我們劃分方式的因素有很多 , 包括不同的文化背景、國家個人、社會階層以及不同的教育背景	and there are a lot of factors that influence the way we divide , including different cultural backgrounds , nations , individuals , social classes ,
問題是由於這些因素的存在 , 最終導致時間洞察力都具是片面的因為你學會經常使用其中的一些 , 而其他的則被很少使用	the problem is that these factors exist , and ultimately , time perspective is shadowy , because you learn to use some of them more often , and others are very few of them .
是什麼促使你做出那些選擇 ?	what makes you make those choices ?
你所做的決定是基於你怎麼採取行動的	the decision you make is based on how you act .
對一些人來說 , 這個決定只是基於現狀另一些人是基於他們的直覺 。	for some people , this decision was based on the status quo , and others based on their intuition .
對於那些基於現狀而做決定的人我們稱呼他們為: " 面向現在 " 因為他們專注於現正發生的事情	for those who make the decisions based on the status quo , we call them " facing now " because they focus on what's happening right now .
對於另一些人來說 , 現正發生什麼並不重要	it doesn't matter what's happening to some other people .
就好像是說: " 我以前好像經歷過類似的事情 " 一樣	it's like saying , " i've been through something like this . "
所以 , 他們基於過去的經驗來做決定	so they're making decisions based on their experiences .
我們稱呼這些人為: " 觀望過去 " , 因為他們專注於過去	we call these people , " look at the past , " because they focus on the past .
還有一部分人 , 他們的考慮不是基於現在 , 也不是過去而是未來	and some of them , not based on the present , not the past , but the future .
他們專注於預期的結果	they focus on the expected outcome .
我們稱呼這些人為:展望未來 。 因為他們專注於將來會是怎麼樣的	we call these people the future , because they're focused on what's going to happen .
那麼 , 時間悖論 , 這裡我要討論的是:時間洞察力的悖論會不會有某個因素影響你做出的每一個決定而你又完全不知 ?	so here's the paradox of time: is there a paradox of time perception that affects every single decision you make that you're completely unaware of ?
那你就具有某種程度上的片面的時間洞察力	so you have some kind of perspective of the time .
實際上是有六種時間洞察力 , 其中兩個屬於 " 面向現在 "	there are actually six kinds of time perspectives , two of which are now .
兩個屬於 " 觀望過去 " , 還有兩個屬於 " 展望未來 "	two belong to the past , and two belong to the future .
你可以專注於 " 積極經歷 " 或 " 消極經歷 "	you can focus on a positive experience or a negative experience .
也可以專注於 " 享受現在 " 指的是你專注於生活中的快樂 , 或者自身宿命這些都無所謂 , 因為你的生活盡在掌握	it can also be focused on enjoying the present , meaning that you're focused on happiness in your life or on your destiny , which doesn't matter , because your life is graspy .
當然 , 你也可以 " 展望未來 " , 設定一個目標	and of course , you can look at the future and set a goal .
或者超越未來指的是:生命在死後重新開始	or beyond the future , meaning that life begins again after death .
透過增強精神靈活性來順利地提升時間洞察力這有賴於環境的需求這就是你要學著去做的	by enhancing flexibility to smoothly enhance the insights that depend on the environment , that's what you learn to do .
那麼 , 什麼是最佳的時間洞察力呢 ?	so what's the best time perspective ?
高度依賴於 " 積極經歷 " , 適度依賴於未來	altitude depends on the positive experience , which depends on future adaptation .
適度依賴於 " 享受現在 "	adaptation depends on enjoying the present .
永遠不考慮 " 消極經歷 " 和 " 宿命論 "	never think about negative experiences and fatalism .
其實 , 最佳的時間洞察力是由你過去的經歷 " 積極經歷 " 奠定了基礎 , 你和你的家庭 , 獨立自主	in fact , the optimal time perspective is laid down by your past experience , your active experience , yours and your families , your own independence .
從未來得到是值得奮鬥的目標 , 新的挑戰	getting from the future is a fighting target , a new challenge .
從 " 享受現在 " 中得到的是動力去探索自身世界、他人以及原始需求	what you get from enjoying the present is the momentum to explore its own world , its other and its original needs .
任何時間洞察力中總是負性多於正性的	insight is always more negative than positive at any given time .
舉個例子:為了將來的成功我們需要犧牲些什麼呢 ?	for instance , what do we need to sacrifice in the future ?
我們需要犧牲和家庭在一起的時光 , 需要犧牲和朋友在一起的時光	we need to sacrifice time with our family when we need to sacrifice time with our friends .
需要犧牲那些快樂的時光 , 需要犧牲個人嗜好	you need to sacrifice those happy times , you need to sacrifice personal hobbies .
需要犧牲業餘愛好 , 需要犧牲睡眠時間 。 因此會影響身體健康	we need to sacrifice hobbies , we need to sacrifice sleep time .
他們的生活中只有工作、成就和控制慾	they only live in work , achievement and control of desire .
我保證你們在座的一些人會對此引起共鳴	i guarantee some of you will resonate with this .
這些與我引起了共鳴 , 我出生於南布朗克斯貧民窟中的一個貧困的西西里島人的家庭中 。 每個人都是在沉<unk>過去和活在當下	it resonated with me , and i was born in a poor sicilian family in the south bronx slum in a ghetto of southern bronx , where everyone was missing out and living right now .

這裡 , 我只是想說:要應用這個原理去解決世界上的很多問題改變學校的退學率打擊毒品 , 增強青少年健康用時間隱喻法治療那些患有創傷後應激障礙的老兵創造醫學奇蹟促進可持續發展和保護在具有50%退出率的醫院內減緩身體康復改變那些呼籲自殺的恐怖分子將家庭矛盾轉化為時間區域的衝突	here , i just want to say that applying this principle to solve many of the world's problems , to change school dropping rates , to enhance teen health metaphors , to treat those traumatic traumatic older soldiers who have posttraumatic stress disorder , to promote sustainability and protect in hospitals with 50 percent exit rates , to mitigate physical rehabilitation , to transform terrorists who are calling for suicide into conflicts in time .

在佈德魯斯我們意識到那堵牆會搶佔我們的土地	in budrus , we realized that the wall was robbing our land .
以色列男子:這堵圍牆事實上是防止恐怖行動的一項解決方法	israeli man: the wall is actually a solution to preventing terrorism .
今天我號召大家加入一場和平的遊行	today , i call on a peace march .
與你們並肩行動的是幾十位以色列兄弟姊妹	working side by side with you dozens of israeli brothers and sisters .
以色列行動主義者:最令軍隊害怕的就是非暴力抵抗	israeli activist: what scares the army most is nonviolent resistance .
